From indianathann at gmail.com  Wed Aug  1 13:35:00 2007
From: indianathann at gmail.com (Padhu Indianathann)
Date: Wed Aug  1 13:35:09 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Double network handling in Single Ethenet card
Message-ID: <e43212340708010105l1c932aacxfff387a8abcafbbf@mail.gmail.com>

In Windows2000,
                       I use Single (realtek) eathernet card for class B and
Class C network without changing IP addresses in Local area connection
TCP/IP address.
That is First, I load Main Static IP by
       Start -->Settings--> My network places--> area connection
Here click properties, In new Window, selecting 'TCP/IP' and press
'Properties'

              192.168.42.3
              255.255.255.0
              192.168.42.100
Keep blank in DNS server addresses. and press Advanced tab,
                  In new Window, I add
Both Class b, C Ip adresses, subnet masks and gate ways.
      Then press ok for each windows (Save and Exit).

After that, In command prompt, I give the following commands,

c:\> route -p add 192.168.0.0 mask 255.255.0.0 192.168.42.100
c:\> route -p add 172.20.0.0 mask 255.255.0.0 172.20.16.1

        Here third IP is Gateway.

 Now system working for both networks. But not at a time for both. U can use
only Class b network and complete the job then u can go to Class C network.
For example, we can browse the web page of only Class b and close it then we
browse class C web page.

   Is it possible in Redhat Linux System?
If it is possible please post the script how to do it.

> eth1

On 8/1/07, Padhu Indianathann <indianathann@gmail.com> wrote:
>    Is it possible in Redhat Linux System?
> If it is possible please post the script how to do it.

You will need to create virtual interface eg. eth0:0
And you will need to enable IP forwarding
echo "1" > /proc/sys/net/ipv4/ip_forward
There's some info on this link
http://www.howtoforge.com/perfect_setup_fedora_core_4

From andyetitmoves at gmail.com  Thu Aug  2 01:17:14 2007
From: andyetitmoves at gmail.com (Ramkumar R. Aiyengar)
Date: Thu Aug  2 01:17:23 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Interfacing Nokia 3110 Classic phone thru USB with Linux
Message-ID: <9a9bfc170708011247k28ba15d1va1ddbe4b47bc9877@mail.gmail.com>

Hi!

[ I sent this mail and I guess it didn't reach the list. So sending
again.. Sorry if it appears in duplicate ]

I got a Nokia 3110 Classic recently and have been running into
problems using it with Linux through the USB (micro USB 2.0) interface
the phone provides...

I use a custom kernel... This is `uname -a`

Linux moonface 2.6.21-viper3 #3 PREEMPT Tue Jun 26 15:23:33 IST 2007
i686 GNU/Linux

I use Debian Testing.

When I connect the device, the mobile detects that it has been
connected, and asks me the mode to choose (Nokia mode/USB
storage/PictBridge). I chose Nokia mode (haven't tested the USB
storage mode as yet as I don't have the add on micro SD card)

dmesg however doesn't seem to get excited...

usb 2-2: new full speed USB device using ohci_hcd and address 8
usb 2-2: configuration #1 chosen from 1 choice

and no further messages...

The userland apps (Gnokii and Gammu) both expect a serial device to
read/write to... I should expect /dev/ttyUSB0 to pop up, udev being
there, but nothing like that happens...

I manually modprobe usbserial, and repeat process... Same results...

This is what lsusb shows

Bus 002 Device 009: ID 0421:005e Nokia Mobile Phones

Taking a cue from Documentation/usb/usb-serial.txt, I rmmod usbserial, and do...

$ modprobe usbserial vendor=0x0421 product=0x005e

I reconnect the device, and this time a lot of messages get thrown up...

usb 2-2: new full speed USB device using ohci_hcd and address 9
usb 2-2: configuration #1 chosen from 1 choice
usbserial_generic 2-2:1.0: generic converter detected
usbserial_generic 2-2:1.0: Generic device with no bulk out, not allowed.
usbserial_generic: probe of 2-2:1.0 failed with error -5

(repeat last three lines for 2-2:1.1 to 2-2:1.9)

usb 2-2: generic converter now attached to ttyUSB1
usbserial_generic 2-2:1.11: generic converter detected
usbserial_generic 2-2:1.11: Generic device with no bulk out, not allowed.
usbserial_generic: probe of 2-2:1.11 failed with error -5

(repeat last three lines for 2-2:1.12 to 2-2:1.14)

/dev/ttyUSB0 and /dev/ttyUSB1 are anyway created and accessible (I am
a member of dialout and gnokii groups), so I try the apps anyway

$ gammu --identify
Error setting device DTR or RTS.

(Error Code: 255)

$ gnokii --identify
GNOKII Version 0.6.14

(and then it hangs there)

Could some one throw light on this?

it moves on...

From shakthimaan at gmail.com  Thu Aug  2 01:48:43 2007
From: shakthimaan at gmail.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Thu Aug  2 01:48:53 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Interfacing Nokia 3110 Classic phone thru USB with Linux
In-Reply-To: <9a9bfc170708011247k28ba15d1va1ddbe4b47bc9877@mail.gmail.com>
References: <9a9bfc170708011247k28ba15d1va1ddbe4b47bc9877@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <d16b1c80708011318n2f62e6dcw5054c0c85da6f08d@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,

On 8/1/07, Ramkumar R. Aiyengar <andyetitmoves@gmail.com> wrote:
> through the USB (micro USB 2.0) interface
> the phone provides...

Did you ask Nokia for the Linux drivers?

> When I connect the device, the mobile detects that it has been
> connected, and asks me the mode to choose (Nokia mode/USB
> storage/PictBridge).

These are the modes in which the phone should operate in.

> dmesg however doesn't seem to get excited...
> usb 2-2: new full speed USB device using ohci_hcd and address 8
> usb 2-2: configuration #1 chosen from 1 choice

Is cdc_acm driver loaded?

> The userland apps (Gnokii and Gammu) both expect a serial device to
> read/write to

That is correct. You might also want to try Wammu:
http://wammu.eu/

>... I should expect /dev/ttyUSB0 to pop up, udev being
> there, but nothing like that happens...

If and only if it presents the Communications Device Class Abstract
Control Model (CDC-ACM) interface to the host.

> I manually modprobe usbserial

Did you modprobe cdc_acm? Do it before you plug the phone.

> This is what lsusb shows
> Bus 002 Device 009: ID 0421:005e Nokia Mobile Phones

Because, USB device enumeration has succeeded.

> usb 2-2: new full speed USB device using ohci_hcd and address 9
> usb 2-2: configuration #1 chosen from 1 choice
> usbserial_generic 2-2:1.0: generic converter detected
> usbserial_generic 2-2:1.0: Generic device with no bulk out, not allowed.

You need BULK OUT and BULK IN endpoints to transfer AT commands and
receive responses.

> usb 2-2: generic converter now attached to ttyUSB1
> usbserial_generic 2-2:1.11: generic converter detected

Install gtkterm or open minicom, and connect to /dev/ttyUSB1. Try to
type AT commands. For example:

AT<hit-enter>
OK
AT+CGMI<hit-enter>
Nokia

> usbserial_generic 2-2:1.11: Generic device with no bulk out, not allowed.

Because the AT command didn't know the unknown BULK OUT endpoint to
send the data to?

SK

-- 
Shakthi Kannan
http://www.shakthimaan.com

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Thu Aug  2 12:53:26 2007
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Thu Aug  2 12:41:20 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] RAM Issue (was: Re: ilugc Digest, Vol 39, Issue 3)
In-Reply-To: <457128.59547.qm@web8907.mail.in.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0708021239430.2954-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

On Thu, 2 Aug 2007, arun kumar wrote:

> I am facing one problem, i cant upgrade my ram, already i am having
> 1 gb i want to crease that to 2gb and i added another 1 gb, the bios
> setting is taking the aditional ram (it is showing 2gb) 

> but the os is not taking to use. so what should i do. OS is DEBIAN

How did you find this? Using 'free' command?

A kernel parameter will help you indicate the RAM to OS.

mem=nn[KMG] [KNL,BOOT] force use of a specific amount of
            memory; to be used when the kernel is not able
            to see the whole system memory or for test.

You have add this in the grub file (/boot/grub/menu.lst)

kernel /vmlinuz-2.4.20-8 ro root=/dev/hda1 mem=2G
                                           ^^^^^^

NOTE: PLZ don't blindly reply to digest mails. Send your query in a
new mail with proper subject line.

Bye :)
--

On 8/2/07, Ramkumar R. Aiyengar <andyetitmoves@gmail.com> wrote:
> Wammu is good, but seems buggy. I need a nice interface for editing
> all fields of my contact list.

To interact with applications, you will need software that can support
SYNCML [1]. Most phones use that. You can also look at Funambol [2].

> I tried gmobilemedia also, but it says my model is not supported. I am
> at a loss to know what it's problem could be, when libgammu doesn't
> have one :)

gammu was forked from gnokii2. I don't like the CamelCase coding
style. It is a strain for my eyes.

> If I don't succeed in finding one, I guess I will in
> typical Linux geekish way end up writing a shell or a perl script :D

There is a cquery Perl script from:

ftp://gatling.ikk.sztaki.hu/pub/samsem/
http://gatling.ikk.sztaki.hu/~kissg/gsm/

It is under public domain.

Get together, invite all ILUGC, users-iitm folks, and ask them to
bring their USB phones. Plug it in on Debian. Test connectivity with
your Perl script. Make the application rock solid. Call it the "Plug
n' Play" project, or give it a good project name.

Have fun,

[1] http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SyncML
[2] http://www.funambol.com/opensource/

Shakthi Kannan

From joscollin at gmail.com  Thu Aug  2 21:56:05 2007
From: joscollin at gmail.com (Jos Collin)
Date: Thu Aug  2 21:56:16 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Number lock on during Linux startup by default.
In-Reply-To: <e43212340708020325h3e93666cm872fdbe3fb23e267@mail.gmail.com>
References: <e43212340708020325h3e93666cm872fdbe3fb23e267@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <95d83d900708020926o63a65d3ar8efea04607354534@mail.gmail.com>

Write the following in /etc/rc.local before the line 'exit 0'
---------------------------------------------
INITTY=/dev/tty[1-8]
for tty in $INITTY; do
        setleds -D +num < $tty
done
-----------------------------------------------


For X you can use

numlockx on

- Jos Collin

From girishvenkatachalam at gmail.com  Fri Aug  3 09:52:32 2007
From: girishvenkatachalam at gmail.com (Girish Venkatachalam)
Date: Fri Aug  3 09:52:51 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] problem with sound recording
In-Reply-To: <69621d830708021108p69c1c78ci98c01ab1c4f7e694@mail.gmail.com>
References: <69621d830708021108p69c1c78ci98c01ab1c4f7e694@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20070803042232.GA6041@lakshmi.susmita.org>

On Fri, Aug 03, 2007 at 12:08:34AM +0600, Zico wrote:
> Hello all..
> 
> One of my friend wants to record some of his voice with microphone in
> debian. He is using *cmi8738 4-channel* sound card.
> He tried with [1] sound-recorder [2] krec [3] audacity. But, his debian
> cannot take input with microphone. Every option of his microphone is on.
> But, he cannot do it. And as i can realize, his microphone is not actually
> taking voices as input but his microphone is ok.
> 
> Can you please help him to do it?
> 

Have you tried unmuting the mic input?

Have you tried with sox? (http://sox.sourceforge.net)?

Did you do a dd or cat of /dev/dsp to a file and try to play with
'play'?

Have you tried recording from line in?

I have never had problems working with sound recording on linux.

I have had noise issues but I could use skype and record voice using a 
microphone.

This sox command line should do it for you.

$ sox -t ossdsp /dev/dsp -w -c 1 -t wav voice.wav

But before that, check your mixer settings with rexima or aumix.

Best of luck!

regards,
Girish

On 03-Aug-07, at 9:52 AM, Girish Venkatachalam wrote:

>> cannot take input with microphone. Every option of his microphone  
>> is on.

that is the mistake - if every option on the mic is on, the input  
from the mic goes to the headset/speakers. In kmix, put the red  
button under the mic on and the green button above the mic off

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Fri Aug  3 13:08:09 2007
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Fri Aug  3 12:56:03 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Mandriva on dealing with M$
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0708031306160.667-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

The interoperability and patent deals between Microsoft and various
Linux distributors and other companies became a hot topic in the Linux
world recently. After several articles were printed speculating that
Mandriva might be the next to sign such a deal, we decided to make a
definitive statement to remove any doubt about the issue: we will not
sign any patent agreement with Microsoft. We believe properly defined,
open industry standards are the best route to interoperability, and
that Microsoft has yet to demonstrate any plausible claims of patent
infringement in Linux. The full statement by Mandriva CEO Francois
Bancilhon is available here:

http://blog.mandriva.com/2007/06/19/we-will-not-go-to-canossa/

Bye :)
--
Bharathi S

Dear Francis,

     I am afraid this is for OpenBSD but it should be very similar.

     http://www.openbsd.org/papers/opencon06-umts/index.html

     The good news is that the firmware does all the dirty work for you
     so the host computer never has to worry about any wireless protocol 
     handling.

     All you have to do is hook up the serial/USB port to use the
     right baud rates and other stuff ( comm bet host and modem).
     
     Best of luck!

regards,
Girish
PS : I dunno any further than this as I have not even seen the
photograph of the hardware you are talking about. :)

On 8/4/07, Dileep M. Kumar <dileep.kumarayil@gmail.com> wrote:
> On 8/3/07, Francis Bosco <ifrbose@gmail.com> wrote:
> > I am using airtel mobile office GPRS net connection in my Motorolla phone.
>
> http://kumarayil.blogspot.com/ . Read the blog GPRS on Fedora 7. Hope
> that helps.
>

Hmm, on my mobile (k750i) I need to specify the airtel gprs APN.
Here's my /etc/wvdial.conf:

[Dialer Defaults]
Init1 = ATZ
Init2 = ATQ0 V1 E1 S0=0 &C1 &D2 +FCLASS=0
Init3 = AT+CGDCONT=1,"IP","airtelgprs.com","",0,0
Stupid Mode = 1
Modem Type = Analog Modem
ISDN = 0
New PPPD = yes
Phone = *99#
Modem = /dev/ttyACM0
Username = crank
Password = bob
Baud = 460800

@francis: Are you looking for bluetooth or USB? Also if you're looking
for a nice graphical way of doing it, you might want to install KPPP.

--Arnold

On 8/5/07, Kenneth Gonsalves <lawgon@thenilgiris.com> wrote:

> On 04-Aug-07, at 2:55 PM, Arnold Noronha wrote:
>
> > Phone = *99#
>
> my airtel dials at *99***1#

The '1' refers to the number of the data-profile as stored in the phone. [1]
So if you have more than one profile, you could use *99***2# for
example. I think *99# should be same as *99***1#

[1] https://help.ubuntu.com/community/BluetoothDialup#head-41f4a1f80eb06226f8939549a534c7b952be69d1

--Arnold

Red Hat has multiple openings for Software Engineers at Pune.

Provided below are the job descriptions along with TAGs which should be
used in $SUBJECT line of the application.

Please ensure that you provide the CV in Open Document Format (ODF) to
sankar {at} redhat {dot} com and jrajopad {at} redhat {dot} com.

For both the openings participation in existing Free and Open Source
projects would be an added advantage.

* Sr Software Engineer (SrSWENGG)

Software engineer with a strong technical background to ensure the
reliability of Red Hat products and services. The primary focus will be
to solicit and prioritize detailed feature requests to support software
portfolios running within the larger Red Hat Enterprise Linux ecosystem.
An ideal candidate would have demonstrated people, project management
experience and excellent communication skills. Other skills include
software skills to develop the test environment, create test automation,
execute functional tests, deliver in depth defect reports

Required Skills:

Knowledge of Standards and Guidelines pertaining to the following:

+ FHS
+ LSB
+ Freedesktop Standards
+ Portland Project Guidelines
+ Packaging Guidelines
+ Knowledge of RPM
+ Python, Ruby
+ GNU Coding Standards
+ Autoconf/Automake
+ GDB

Profile:

o 5+ years work experience with a designing, coding, debugging, and
deploying software in a leadership role.
o Firm foundation in at least one object oriented programming language
(Python or Ruby) with some experience of other technologies, scripting
languages, databases and software engineering. (essential)
o Robust experience of *nix /APIs/ ABI compatibility. (essential)
o An understanding of how commercial software fits into an Open Source
world.
o Deep understanding of FHS, LSB, GNU coding standards, Guidelines.
(Essential)
o Strong proficiency with RPM and RPM specfile syntax.
o Understanding of configuration management principles.
o Must understand the general software development release cycle, source
management and defect management methodologies in Linux environment.

* Associate Software Engineer (ASWENGG)

Software engineer with a strong technical background to ensure the
reliability of Red Hat products and services. The primary focus will be
to solicit and prioritize detailed feature requests to support software
portfolios running within the larger Red Hat Enterprise Linux ecosystem.
An ideal candidate would have demonstrated people, project management
experience and excellent communication skills. Other skills include
software skills to develop the test environment, create test automation,
execute functional tests, deliver in depth defect reports

Required Skills:

Knowledge of Standards and Guidelines pertaining to the following:

+ FHS
+ Packaging Guidelines
+ Knowledge of RPM
+ Python, Ruby
+ GNU Coding Standards
+ Autoconf/Automake
+ GDB

Profile:

o 1+ years work experience with a designing, coding, debugging software
o Firm foundation in at least one object oriented programming language
(Python or Ruby) with some experience of other technologies, scripting
languages, databases and software engineering. (essential)
o Robust experience of *nix /APIs/ ABI compatibility. (essential)
o Strong proficiency with RPM and RPM specfile syntax.
o Understanding of configuration management principles.
o Must understand the general software development release cycle, source
management and defect management methodologies in Linux environment.

by usual PATH precedes the debian gedit in /usr/bin. So, typing gedit
will end up running your compiled executable.

While checking the web, i found a suggestion to use mkinitrd.yaird instead
of initramfs. The resultant image of using this command was only 1/4
the size of the other initrd image and it did not even come till my
previous booting stage.
Another suggestion was to put a sleep command in the init script of
initrd image before the "mountroot" command. This also did not work as
it resulted in the same problem.

Mine is a SATA harddisk and I understand this is a problem related to
the sata disk.

Can someone help to solve this problem?

thanks,
siva.
From f2005180 at bits-pilani.ac.in  Tue Aug  7 17:37:03 2007
From: f2005180 at bits-pilani.ac.in (Karthik Ramgopal)
Date: Tue Aug  7 17:39:37 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Firefox 2 and fc6
In-Reply-To: <20070807115004.64C6F1DB27F@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
References: <20070807115004.64C6F1DB27F@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
Message-ID: <000001c7d8eb$817fa990$847efcb0$@ac.in>

Fedora core 6 doesn't have firefox 2 rpm's officially compiled. If you wanna
get firefox 2.0 for fc6, you have two options

1. compile from source
2. Add remi repo to yum.repos.d and then do a yum update firefox

http://remi.collet.free.fr/rpms/remi.repo

Regards,
Karthik Ramgopal
BITS Pilani

Hi,

On 8/7/07, Sivaram Kannan <siva.devel@gmail.com> wrote:
> "waiting for root file system".

I've seen that too.

> While checking the web, i found a suggestion to use mkinitrd.yaird instead
> of initramfs. The resultant image of using this command was only 1/4
> the size of the other initrd image

Yes.

> Mine is a SATA harddisk and I understand this is a problem related to
> the sata disk.

Some searching in Google resulted in info that udev was not updated
properly. So, you have to boot from a LiveCD, chroot, do apt-get
update, upgrade. This should fix udev. Now, you can reboot to the
newly built kernel and ramdisk image, and this is supposed to work.

No LiveCD here to try it though.

SK

On 8/7/2007 6:26 PM, Shakthi Kannan wrote:

> Some searching in Google resulted in info that udev was not updated
> properly. So, you have to boot from a LiveCD, chroot, do apt-get
> update, upgrade. This should fix udev. Now, you can reboot to the
> newly built kernel and ramdisk image, and this is supposed to work.
>

Or it hasn't been able to find the module for your root fs

1. Generate system.map and make sure it is being checked from grub

and/or

2. Compile the module for your root fs (say ext3) into your kernel
instead of as a module.

practical  advice than any other book i have seen ,  along with what happens
in the  server rooms and what are the things most needed for any sys admin (
including a pack of Beer  cans :-) )  but if you are looking for an
introduction to linux , get a book from teach your self series from sams

8) Contribute Compatible for Dreamweaver
9) DB >50mb[approx]

Tamil Nadu schools go for SUSE Linux 
The exodus is to eliminate numerous proprietary software licenses and
reduce hardware costs 
MUMBAI, INDIA: The Electronics Corporation of Tamil Nadu (ELCOT) is
rolling out SUSE Linux
<http://www.ciol.com/content/developer/Linux/2006/106071801.asp>
Enterprise across 30,000 desktops and 1,880 servers in Tamil Nadu's
schools. Earlier, ELCOT had migrated its entire IT infrastructure from
Microsoft Windows to the SUSE Linux Enterprise Server and SUSE Linux
Enterprise Desktop from Novell.


"The open source software in SUSE Linux Enterprise is superb," said C.
Umashankar, managing director of ELCOT. "In addition, we estimate that
moving to Linux has reduced our general hardware costs by nearly 25
percent. In case of high-end servers
<http://www.ciol.com/content/860797344.aspx> , the savings could be as
much as 80 percent. What's more important is the benefits that the Tamil
Nadu's students will get from this. There is a growing trend towards the
corporate adoption of Linux, both in India and elsewhere. So it will be
a real advantage in the job market to have experience working with open
source software. It gives us tremendous freedom and choice," he added.


ELCOT has been procuring hardware and software for the various
departments of the Government of Tamil Nadu, which serves a population
of more than 70 million, since 1977. ELCOT's main objective is to offer
the best possible IT solutions at the lowest price, thus maximizing the
return on investment of public money, says a release from the company.
ELCOT is also involved in consulting, implementation, support and
training to help meet the state's ambitious e-governance objectives.


Before the rollout of SUSE Linux Enterprise to the schools and
government offices across Tamil Nadu, ELCOT first migrated its own
in-house IT systems to Linux for its user-friendly, cost-effective and
security reasons, says the release. The organization then worked with
teachers to design a pre-loaded set of applications which could be
delivered to the 30,000 new PCs along with SUSE Linux Enterprise
Desktop. ELCOT also rolled out SUSE Linux Enterprise Server to the
schools' 1,880 servers, which are now 100 percent Linux-based.


Roger Levy, senior vice president and general manager of Open Platform
Solutions, Novell, said, "ELCOT was able to eliminate tens of thousands
of proprietary software licenses by moving to open source software
<http://www.ciol.com/content/developer/Linux/2007/107041801.asp> , in
addition to their tremendous savings from making better use of hardware
resources. The decision to move to a new platform rests not only on
immediate pricing considerations, but also on the potential long-term
hardware, software and infrastructure costs. Based on these criteria,
SUSE Linux Enterprise is proving its value to customers around the
world."


The next-generation platform for the open enterprise, SUSE Linux
Enterprise is the best-engineered, lowest-cost and most interoperable
platform for enterprise computing, from the desktop to the data center,
according to the release.

my view is that you can go for a dedicated server and configure everything
yourself( if u r a hacker ) or else go where they do shared hosting... in
the dedicated environment you dont have to depend on others( except for
network and system failure) .. dedicated works out well in the department of
reliability( depends on the app pgmrs and the admin ) but not economical(
until you are very specific) .. you can at max put 2 servers and host close
to 10 websites depending on the traffic and system configuration...

Suresh Ramasubramanian wrote:
> If you want someone with bandwidth exclusively from some cheaper outfit
> like cogent or pccwbtn .. and "data centers" that are a closet in some
> carrier hotel - sure, you get cheap that way. You might even find that
> it works for you just fine.

whats more important than who you get your b/w from is how your peerings
work, and how your clientbase accepts that. Getting cheaper connections
does not mean they are going to be worse. And you will also find in this
business, like most, smaller companies are more likely to accommodate
specific requirements. eg. its easier for me to get direct peering with
$BigAssHostingCompany working with a 5 man outfit than it is for me to
get savvis to jump their LINX endpoint and give me a direct link, so i
dont pay for transit when my webservers in the DC on the West Coast, USA
hit the db servers sitting in my office in London, UK.

> But if you are looking at the kind of bandwidth he was talking about..

I must have missed something, since he only seemed to want a few
gigs/month in the OP. which works down to a few dozen kb/sec in link
assurance.

the only sort of hosting providers who are going to struggle with that
are the ones who run their server from their bedroom on the adsl link
that their dad's pay for.

From animeshs at gmail.com  Thu Aug  9 19:34:54 2007
From: animeshs at gmail.com (Animesh Singh)
Date: Thu Aug  9 19:35:06 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Partition information lost on reboot.
In-Reply-To: <00a701c7da84$00882890$140110ac@LOGUCO>
References: <c021e3c90708090445o510dba60n830226ea6f8acce3@mail.gmail.com>
	<00a701c7da84$00882890$140110ac@LOGUCO>
Message-ID: <e8fef13b0708090704p7003e585x2d1540df102ab02a@mail.gmail.com>

> To give more information on this, Initially there were two SCSI disks
> connected to a hardware HostRaid (Adaptec ASC-29320 U320) adapter.
> And it was configured for RAID-0 (Striping). Each conneted disk was of 73
> GB.
>
> When I issued fdisk -l on the system it showed both sda and sdb as 73 GB
> each. I did not know (the device name) how to access the disk as RAID?. I
Well it made it clear that you have not configured HW raid.
(So, I'm assuming that "sda" & "sdb" is a real drive and not some
pseudo-drive which exists only in the firmware of the RAID
controller.)

Paste the output of "cat /proc/mdstat" after reboot and before you run
partprobe and second after you run partprobe.

> I would be greatful it if I get the information for the three questions.
>
> 1. what should be done access the disks as raid
mdadm --examine --scan  /dev/sda1 /dev/sda2 > /etc/mdadm.conf
Edit /etc/mdadm.conf so that the devices statements are on the same
lines as the ARRAY statements, as they are in below listing.  Add the
"missing" device to the devices entry for each array member to fill
out the raid1 complement of two devices per array. Don't forget to
renumber the md entries if the recovery computer already has md
devices and ARRAY statements in /etc/mdadm.conf

Listing: DEVICE partitions

ARRAY /dev/md0 level=raid1 num-devices=2
 ?UUID=b3cd99e7:d02be486:b0ea429a:e18ccf65
 ?devices=/dev/sda1,missing
ARRAY /dev/md1 level=raid1 num-devices=2
 ?UUID=75fa22aa:9a11bcad:b42ed14a:b5f8da3c
 ?devices=/dev/sda2,missing

Then, activate the new md devices with mdadm -A -s, and check
/proc/mdstat to verify that the RAID array is active.

Note: Above config depends how you have built it up.


> 2. why is it saying /dev/sda1 is used by the system even though the HW RAID
> configuration is disabled in the BIOS and no one is using it. (tried fuser
> and lsof)
It was never in BIOS ( see above comment ) and fuser & lsof works only
for user space.

> 3. What is the reason for the partition not being detected automatically
> with single disk.
probable disk partitioninformation is not stored in a right way on
disk and the bootup commands out of box linux, does not have command
to retrive partition information.


Animesh.

Message-ID: <loom.20070810T095849-997@post.gmane.org>

Animesh Singh <animeshs@...> writes:
> > To give more information on this, Initially there were two SCSI disks
> > connected to a hardware HostRaid (Adaptec ASC-29320 U320) adapter.
> > And it was configured for RAID-0 (Striping). Each conneted disk was of 73
> > GB.
> >
> > When I issued fdisk -l on the system it showed both sda and sdb as 73 GB
> > each. I did not know (the device name) how to access the disk as RAID?. I
> Well it made it clear that you have not configured HW raid.
> (So, I'm assuming that "sda" & "sdb" is a real drive and not some
> pseudo-drive which exists only in the firmware of the RAID
> controller.)

come on luggies, we need to give better advice to this user. i suppose this is
better than the previous advice which was to run fsck! please try to understand
the problem before giving out solutions. adaptec hostraid is pseudo raid and it
is not possible to do hardware raid with this (meaning, adaptec's drivers will
give you equivalent of software raid functionality and that is all you can do);
when that is enabled, all drives will be pseudo drives only existing in the
firmware of the raid controller. but then, since the card only provides software
raid equivalent, the advice to switch to software raid (md device) provided by
the kernel is actually valid advice! it would appear that there is some problem
with the partition table being read by the system. it may be possible to clear
that by setting the card to straight scsi mode (disabling all hostraid
functionality), deleting all partitions from the partition table, rebooting and
then creating fresh partition table entries.

sriram

From ambuj.mbp at gmail.com  Fri Aug 10 23:20:55 2007
From: ambuj.mbp at gmail.com (Ambuj Thacker)
Date: Fri Aug 10 23:21:05 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Partition information lost on reboot.
Message-ID: <c021e3c90708101050l50678333wdbc1623b524c55e5@mail.gmail.com>

You have 2 hard disks(sda,sdb).
You can create software raid by-:
=>mdadm -C /dev/md0 --chunk=64 --level=1 --raid-devices=2 /dev/sda /dev/sdb
=>issue cat /proc/mdstat to see the raid device running
=> mkfs -t ext3 /dev/md0
=> mount /dev/md0 /mount_RAID
If there was an problem in creating RAID then I think(not sure) you will
have to recreate s/w raid.But if its under LVM  you can extend it and try to
add sdb.
You can mount /dev/sda or /dev/sdb (if /dev/md0 is not mounted) on other
directory and check for the empty space(as it is RAID0->stripping mode data
is stored in both the devices)

I think in /etc/fstab there is no entry for /dev/md* which is creating
problem in mounting the devices.Try entering
/dev/md0      /mount_RAID        ext3     defaults    0 0

You can find about raid in kernel dmesg by
# dmesg | grep RAID
# less /proc/kcore |strings|grep RAID>~/data.txt (This command will take
time)
will also give you some information about raid.

Do tell us how did you create s/w raid and the empty space/occupied memory
in sda and sdb.If I have misunderstood your problem then inform us.

aMBUJ
   :?
P.S: I am not sure whether it will solve your problem or not but if it works
kindly let me know.

Date: Sat Aug 11 17:21:27 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] How to recover root Password in Solaris
In-Reply-To: <983163.7581.qm@web52907.mail.re2.yahoo.com>
References: <7E7874E9-7B69-438C-A7C4-FCA2AC9F15BA@thenilgiris.com>
	<983163.7581.qm@web52907.mail.re2.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <3e4fd9970708110451w5af23947w799c03cfa4187bca@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,

On 8/8/07, Deepak Dikshit <dd_midas@yahoo.com> wrote:
> Dear All,
> I want to recover the root password of one of my Solaris server(I think, any linux mechanism will work here too). Last used password is either changed accidently or expired.
> Any kind of help or pointer will be highly appreciated.

No gaurantee but you can try this.
1) Boot solaris installed machine with linux live cd.
2) Mount the root filesystem.
3) edit /etc/passwd and set root passwd to blank
4) boot into solaris, press enter when prompted for root password
5) if login happens, immediately change root password

WARNING: This mechanism has worked on linux but not gauranteed to work
on Solaris. Tyr it on your own risk. This method might cause root to
be locked out for ever.

reagrds
VK

Init2 = ATQ0 V1 E1 S0=0 &C1 &D2 +FCLASS=0
Modem Type = USB Modem
Phone = *99***1#
ISDN = 0
Username = " "
Init1 = ATZ
Password = " "
Modem = /dev/ttyACM0
Baud = 460800

Subject: [Ilugc] How to recover root Password in Solaris
In-Reply-To: <3e4fd9970708110451w5af23947w799c03cfa4187bca@mail.gmail.com>
References: <7E7874E9-7B69-438C-A7C4-FCA2AC9F15BA@thenilgiris.com>

	<3e4fd9970708110451w5af23947w799c03cfa4187bca@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <e5a77ac20708122257u3fd1a4fdw196906e7cd38e63f@mail.gmail.com>

On 8/11/07, vivek khurana <mailing.vivek@gmail.com> wrote:
>
> Hi,
>
> On 8/8/07, Deepak Dikshit <dd_midas@yahoo.com> wrote:
> > Dear All,
> > I want to recover the root password of one of my Solaris server(I think,
> any linux mechanism will work here too). Last used password is either
> changed accidently or expired.
> > Any kind of help or pointer will be highly appreciated.
>
> No gaurantee but you can try this.
> 1) Boot solaris installed machine with linux live cd.
> 2) Mount the root filesystem.
> 3) edit /etc/passwd and set root passwd to blank
> 4) boot into solaris, press enter when prompted for root password
> 5) if login happens, immediately change root password
>
> WARNING: This mechanism has worked on linux but not gauranteed to work
> on Solaris. Tyr it on your own risk. This method might cause root to
> be locked out for ever.
>

If your system is sparc based ans Solaris Installation CD/DVD is available
with you then you can follow these steps to reset root password

http://www.softpanorama.org/Solaris/Security/solaris_root_password_recovery.shtml

On 7/25/07, Kenneth Gonsalves <lawgon@thenilgiris.com> wrote:
>
>
> On 25-Jul-07, at 12:15 PM, Sathya narayana wrote:
>
> >  Am trying to convert any tamil text that is in TAM/TAB format to
> > UNICODE.
> > Can anyone help me on this.


TAM and TAB are in 7 bit format.. To convert to Unicode use Python..
I got a logic to covert. Read the file that contains TAM or TAB characters
character by charater prints its equavalent in the terminal..

For example take 'L' is the TAM Character for *?.. *
if c=='L':
      print u'*?'*
**
**
The problem here will be.. Two or Three character of TAM will form a single
charater of Unicode then use nested If statements..
Finally copy the contents in the terminal to a text editor and save it as
unicode file..
thats it

Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Partition information lost on reboot.
References: <c021e3c90708090445o510dba60n830226ea6f8acce3@mail.gmail.com><00a701c7da84$00882890$140110ac@LOGUCO><e8fef13b0708090704p7003e585x2d1540df102ab02a@mail.gmail.com>
	<loom.20070810T095849-997@post.gmane.org>
Message-ID: <010401c7de71$7c703e70$140110ac@LOGUCO>


> come on luggies, we need to give better advice to this user. i suppose 
> this is
> better than the previous advice which was to run fsck! please try to 
> understand
> the problem before giving out solutions. adaptec hostraid is pseudo raid 
> and it
> is not possible to do hardware raid with this (meaning, adaptec's drivers 
> will
> give you equivalent of software raid functionality and that is all you can 
> do);
> when that is enabled, all drives will be pseudo drives only existing in 
> the
> firmware of the raid controller. but then, since the card only provides 
> software
> raid equivalent, the advice to switch to software raid (md device) 
> provided by
> the kernel is actually valid advice! it would appear that there is some 
> problem
> with the partition table being read by the system. it may be possible to 
> clear
> that by setting the card to straight scsi mode (disabling all hostraid
> functionality), deleting all partitions from the partition table, 
> rebooting and
> then creating fresh partition table entries.
>

Thank you for the detailed explanation.
They system is already up with a single disk on production. I will follow 
your procedure when we get them for some kind of maintenance.

Thanks
-logu

> >
> > *wvdial.conf file*
> >
> > [Dialer Defaults]

I modified Init1 to AT&FX1L1 and commented Init2. It works fine. I use
N70 and airtel GPRS on Fedora7.

[dileep@param ~]$ cat /etc/wvdial.conf
[Dialer Defaults]
        Modem = /dev/ttyACM0
        Baud = 57600
        Init = AT&FX1L1
        Phone = *99#
        Username = ""
        Password = ""

Hash: SHA1

Siva Subramaniam wrote:

>               I am working on a GTK project where i have the requirement to
> change the SCIM language whenever user make an action(click a button) and
> that get effected when user types  in a text box. What is the possible way
> to do this?

SCIM (I think if I recall correct) can be triggered by the Ctrl+Space
(default) trigger and the input methods can be changed by various
configurable hotkeys - do you plan to (re)use them or add functionality
in your application over and above this ? Or, is it like a particular
button in your application is proposed to be the trigger through
ClickButton (example) for a SCIM IM change ? Best would be to read the
SCIM docs to figure how to tie in your event with registering it as a
SCIM trigger.

From lawgon at thenilgiris.com  Thu Aug 16 12:22:43 2007
From: lawgon at thenilgiris.com (Kenneth Gonsalves)
Date: Thu Aug 16 12:22:46 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] man in the middle attack?
Message-ID: <5180DEEC-6DD3-42FF-BB3C-9FF05D33D077@thenilgiris.com>

hi,

an installation with two PCs running Mandriva 2007. Connected to the  
net through an airtel routerr/modem. Modem address is 192.168.1.1 and  
the two machines are 192.168.1.2 and 3. The two machines share files  
over ssh. sshd is running on both machines. This morning when the  
machines were switched on - both reported 'ssh fingerprint changed  
and is different from that in .ssh/knownhosts. Suspect man in middle  
attack blah blah'. When the line referring to the host is removed, it  
first adds the address to the list of known hosts - but then a  
message saying ssh authentication disabled as man in the middle  
attack suspected. I am in Chennai and the setup in Coimbatore so this  
info is got over the phone. Both machines are also running shorewall  
with the sshd port open. Any clues?
-- 

regards
kg
http://lawgon.livejournal.com
http://nrcfosshelpline.in/web/


From vaidhy at gmail.com  Thu Aug 16 12:40:32 2007
From: vaidhy at gmail.com (Vaidhyanathan Mayilrangam Gopalan)
Date: Thu Aug 16 12:42:22 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] man in the middle attack?
In-Reply-To: <5180DEEC-6DD3-42FF-BB3C-9FF05D33D077@thenilgiris.com>
References: <5180DEEC-6DD3-42FF-BB3C-9FF05D33D077@thenilgiris.com>
Message-ID: <46C3F868.5010203@gmail.com>

This could happen if the ssh packages in the machine were updated, their 
ip address changed etc. In this case, I suspect that the modem was set 
to dhcp and the machines are usually 2 and 3. Today morning, it could 
have been 3 and 2. Either way, you need to delete the lines in the known 
hosts for all machines that have the same IP and try it again.

Regards,
Vaidhy

> Kenneth Gonsalves wrote:
>> hi,
>> an installation with two PCs running Mandriva 2007. Connected to  
>> the net through an airtel routerr/modem. Modem address is  
>> 192.168.1.1 and the two machines are 192.168.1.2 and 3. The two  
>> machines share files over ssh. sshd is running on both machines.  
>> This morning when the machines were switched on - both reported  
>> 'ssh fingerprint changed and is different from that in .ssh/ 
>> knownhosts. Suspect man in middle attack blah blah'. When the line  
>> referring to the host is removed, it first adds the address to the  
>> list of known hosts - but then a message saying ssh authentication  
>> disabled as man in the middle attack suspected. I am in Chennai  
>> and the setup in Coimbatore so this info is got over the phone.  
>> Both machines are also running shorewall with the sshd port open.  
>> Any clues?

> This could happen if the ssh packages in the machine were updated,  
> their ip address changed etc. In this case, I suspect that the  
> modem was set to dhcp and the machines are usually 2 and 3. Today  
> morning, it could have been 3 and 2. Either way, you need to delete  
> the lines in the known hosts for all machines that have the same IP  
> and try it again.

yes, they got interchanged - i am now hardcoding the addresss

as one of the lines:
/usr/lib/python2.4/lib-dynload/readline.so

(python2.4 in this case). It's also there for python2.5.

So, which latest version of Python are you trying to install?

From arnstein87 at gmail.com  Fri Aug 17 16:32:24 2007
From: arnstein87 at gmail.com (Arnold Noronha)
Date: Fri Aug 17 16:32:39 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] How to make BSNL Dial up connection from Ubuntu
In-Reply-To: <c77544c50708162328s12fe299che223577afdb37bd9@mail.gmail.com>
References: <c77544c50708162328s12fe299che223577afdb37bd9@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <3c52da3c0708170402m3df1d526o4d42a5d8adb028ab@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,

On 8/17/07, Francis Bosco <ifrbose@gmail.com> wrote:
>       My friend using BSNL Dial up connection from Windows system. Now
> he wants to switch over to linux. I have installed Ubuntu on his
> system. But we are not able to connect to the internet. How to make
> dial up connections in Ubuntu/Linux. Can anyone here help me on this?
>

Easiest (but command line way, assuming ubuntu install CD comes with wvdial):

# sudo apt-get install wvdial
# sudo wvdialconf
<output.... hopefully you have only one modem device, if the modem is
not detected you're in trouble (internal winmodem?)>

# sudo vi /etc/wvdial.conf
Edit the username, password and phone number fields and remove the
semi-colon ";" in front of them.

At least earlier, I've found that for dialling to BSNL you need to
disable "Check for dialtone".So add the line:
Abort on no dialtone = off

If you're having problems with GUI's like KPPP, try to disable dialtone check.

HTH

--Arnold

Hi,

My thoughts below:

On 8/17/07, Sudhir Gandotra ( ????? ????????? ) <sudhir@openlx.com> wrote:
> I have
> interviewed over 300 RHCE certified people to get only frustrated.

And it shouldn't have taken you more than 5 minutes to tell how bad they are.

> Seems
> the standards are falling.

They really have no clue how high the Industry standards and
requirements are when you are competing on an International scale.

> I wish the Freshers start realising the need
> of apprenticeship and take a practical down-to-earth approach to career.

There is a problem with the mindset.

* School kids think if they get good marks, they will get into MBBS or
engineering. Atleast they are made to think like that, by mugging up
answers and vomiting in exams. End of the day, they fail to gain any
knowledge/skill.

* College students think if they do well in a job interview, they can
get a job, and life is happy. They don't get any theoretical or
practical hands-on experience or knowledge during their college days
at all!

They don't realize that if they don't have the skills, they cannot do
anything at work. Nobody is going to keep you or pay you if you don't
do any work. You can sit in the bench in the industry without doing
any work, but, it is not going to help your profile or your
credibility in the long run. Only at work do they realize that they
have wasted their life in college. So, some start to work in the
industry in India and it takes them atleast 3-4 years to get a hang of
it, and few more years to become pro. So, this is roughly around the
age of 26-28.

On the contrary, I have seen kids in school in the US turning pro in
college (at the age of 18-20), doing really cool FOSS stuff. Yes, they
all have their own laptops (quite opposite in India). I guess it is
the same in the EU as well. So, you can really see the digital divide.

I have observed the lack of attitude in all the colleges that I have
been to in India. There are very, very few exceptional students. Sorry
if I sound harsh, but, welcome to reality.

SK

-- 
Shakthi Kannan
http://www.shakthimaan.com

@Sudhir
>What you can do is the most important thing.
No doubt about it.

>I have interviewed over 300 RHCE certified people to get only frustrated.
If the interview is for a development job I think RHCE is not the
certification. If it is for administration then RHCE`s do have a chance.

>I wish the Freshers start realising the need of apprenticeship and take a
practical down-to-earth approach to career.
Easily said than done. Freshers try hard to work as an apprentice.But they
fail to obtain one.

@SK
>They don't realize that if they don't have the skills, they cannot do
anything at work.
There cannot be any doubt over it.

engineering. Atleast they are made to think like that, by mugging up answers
and vomiting in exams.
If the mugging and vomiting is pointed to RHCE then yes you have to PRACTICE
a lot to get comfortable with the RHEL environment and commands.

@Sudhir
>The students(looking only at a 50k job to start with, and not bother about
becoming a good human being who also earns good money)
Why the students are targeted???? Its the company who make closed systems
not the students..All of us (I am a student too) are good human being. Every
one wants to keep his environment clean and tidy. But do other professionals
allow it?? Moreover we ,students want to come parallel to our fellow US
students and buy a apple laptop(1.10L) within 3 months of job. Earning money
is not bad (rather its necessary in present conditions) but its bad if it is
earned in a wrong way.

>where they left the "meaning of life" behind, stopped serious-thinking and
just ran after money
This is really bad and I would LOVE to HATE such students :#

be a plus point but not the ace card. Why would a company select anyone if
he is of no use to that company!!! I am sure even RedHat would not hire such
a guy.

A good selection procedure should see the capability and willingness to work
and learn in the candidate.His work in the past always shows his capability.

I apologize for my harshness. But this is what I felt.

> They don't realize that if they don't have the skills, they cannot do
> anything at work. Nobody is going to keep you or pay you if you don't
> do any work. You can sit in the bench in the industry without doing
> any work, but, it is not going to help your profile or your
> credibility in the long run.
Honestly, not many people seem to care as long as they have their
bread made. The industries should teach the lesson by not hiring
incompetence. They won't since they badly need head count. Almost that
is all they need : head count, nothing more.

> On the contrary, I have seen kids in school in the US turning pro in
> college (at the age of 18-20), doing really cool FOSS stuff. Yes, they
> all have their own laptops (quite opposite in India). I guess it is
> the same in the EU as well. So, you can really see the digital divide.

This is something I hate. We should have numbers. Let us talk in terms
of the number of kids in US hacking away the linux kernels to the
number of indian kids hanging around near satyam and citi centres
during college. Geeks are everywhere; so are others. Just that geeks
in america can afford internet, because his dad managed it. Even if
our dads managed it, a good connection is at our disposal only in the
last couple of years. So, no point saying we don't start early. We do.
But to make ourselves known is too damn costly.

people need to use their guts to break the chains of "lacks" around them
and work hard to grow beyond these limitations. That will show them the

not dependents when they have to find girl-friends and boy-friends; they
are not dependent when they have to search for a new toy (cell, game or
whatever), then, why depend about building career and life ?

Hi,

Thanks for all your valuable thoughts. I don't know how valuable this
discussion is for newbies. Anyways, my thoughts below:

--- Ambuj Thacker >ambuj.mbp at gmail.com> wrote:
> hy the students are targeted???? Its the company who make closed systems
> not the students.

There is no relation. As a student, what you are as a person is more
important than who your teachers are, which school you went to, which
company you work for. They are not related. Who you are as a person
makes what you are, not where you are from and which school you went
to or for whom you work. This is where I see high-context cultures,
like India, trying to relate to each other. IMO, there is no relation.

When students put this dependancy on their plight on teachers, the
college, they lose confidence. They think it is their fate. What they
fail to realize is that by using FOSS on their old PII or PIII x86
boxes, they can still do shell programming, GUI development, embedded
development, and learn a lot. So, they never make an effort in the
first place.

> one wants to keep his environment clean and tidy. But do other professionals
> allow it??

Just because there are evil people around, doesn't mean you should
turn into one.

> Moreover we ,students want to come parallel to our fellow US
> students and buy a apple laptop(1.10L) within 3 months of job.

Really? Of all the freshers that I have worked with in the past three
years, the first thing they buy with a big salary is a cell phone, a
bike, spend all the weekends in pubs, going out on old Mahabalipuram
road on weekends to party. Not one, I repeat, not one I have seen buy
a personal computer to work. Even if they did, I'd suspect they will
still use it for gaming or watching movies.

I am not saying that you shouldn't spend on all these. Once in a while
its ok, but, not wasting money every weekend.

On 8/18/07, Ingenieur <goda.abishek@gmail.com> wrote:
> This is something I hate.

Like it or not that is reality.

> We should have numbers.

Every college in the US has ethernet jacks in the classrooms, where
students can plug-in their laptops during class hours. There is also
wireless LAN to which you can connect to. Every class has a projector
that professors can connect their laptops to and can use it during
class sessions. All assignments/lab reports are sent through e-mails.
Classes are also held through voice conferences. All this some 5 years
back when I was studying in the US.

Can you tell me how many colleges in India have these, today? Now, we
are talking numbers.

I still see students in India "writing" homework and assignments. I
have not seen any company in India asking their employees to write
hand written reports to their clients. So you can see that they are
not being trained for anything.

If you have not experienced real education abroad, don't even think of
commenting about it.

> Let us talk in terms
> of the number of kids in US hacking away the linux kernels

I said FOSS not Linux kernels.

> to the
> number of indian kids hanging around near satyam and citi centres
> during college.

I know why Indian kids hang around near Satyam and Citi centers.

> Just that geeks
> in america can afford internet, because his dad managed it. Even if
> our dads managed it, a good connection is at our disposal only in the
> last couple of years.

I agree. That is what I meant by digital divide.

> So, no point saying we don't start early.

Like it or not, that is reality!

> We do.
> But to make ourselves known is too damn costly.

That is what I meant by digital divide.

Cheers,

SK

From girishvenkatachalam at gmail.com  Mon Aug 20 02:03:44 2007
From: girishvenkatachalam at gmail.com (Girish Venkatachalam)
Date: Sun Aug 19 19:05:14 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Mplayer Via-unichrome
In-Reply-To: <661385.52893.qm@web57106.mail.re3.yahoo.com>
References: <661385.52893.qm@web57106.mail.re3.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <20070819203344.GA5610@lakshmi.susmita.org>

On Sat, Aug 18, 2007 at 03:23:53PM +0100, Anurag wrote:
> ppl,
> I have a K8M800 Via unichrome based Desktop, I installed the Mplayer 1pre8 on FC6(x64) but mplayer says it can't find any vidix driver. I checked the xorg.conf file, it says that its using via driver not the vesa driver. So actually it should work out of the box, ain't it.
> 
> How to troubleshoot this....?
> 

$ mplayer -vo help

Does it list xv?

It is not a good idea to try vidix(not mature yet) when the card's
native driver supports the XVideo extension.

mplayer rocks with hardware scaling in the graphic card's GPU, but then
it can also work well if your CPU is good enough using software scaling.

$ mplayer -vo x11 -vf spp,scale=1024:768 video.avi

The SDL,gl and other output drivers work well for me too.

Try

$ xvinfo

or 

$ xdpyinfo | grep -i xvideo

Best,
Girish

> Every college in the US has ethernet jacks in the classrooms, where

remain out of common reach. Was there a step taken in that direction?

I think the important points are :
# IT Engineer has completed his studies.
# He belongs to those 60% that do not get jobs (not that the rest 40%
got the right jobs, but let's first look at those who are still without
jobs)
# This engineer thinks he/she has the degree so the companies should
give the job. Companies think otherwise and this gets proven in the
interviews.
# Where does this Engineer go from here ?

Its a dead-lock that needs to be broken. Surely some creative way will
need to be found for this. Who should be at the forefront, leading the
solution-finding in this situation ?
What is the role of the Engineer in this situation ?
Why does this Engineer, who is without job, not adapt a positive
attitude of doing something here, leading the situation towards a
resolution ?
Surely, if they do it, others will support them, help them find a
solution. I will for sure.
Let's think about this; stop sulking and find a way out.
These Engineers are a rich resource of society and our common social
responsibility (provided of-course, those that want it) and we need to
work out a solution.

--

From raamanp at yahoo.co.in  Mon Aug 20 12:18:55 2007
From: raamanp at yahoo.co.in (Raman.P)
Date: Mon Aug 20 12:19:01 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Two day workshop in Mepco Engg college - Sivakasi
Message-ID: <361706.21637.qm@web7911.mail.in.yahoo.com>

Dear luggies

  I, with Ponnusamy of NRCFOSS did two day workshop on FOSS called
Lynx-07 in Mepco Engg College, Sivakasi.It was organised by the
students under Indian Society for Technical Education - Mepco
Chapter.

  The workshop was for 30 students of CS and IT branches. All were
final year students. Students practiced then and there, as it was
done in one of their labs. A brilliant set of students picking up
well.

  The awarness level is very low. But in two days they seem to be
enthused enough. I am sure FOSS will pickup in the college. 

   The students promised to start a campus lug soon and pass on
knowledge to their juniors. I am hopeful about it.

   On behalf of ILUGC, I thank, Raghav Preethi, Aswin and others of
ISTE-Mepco for organising the workshop. I should also thank the two
seniors who left the college who were instrumental in arranging this.



Raman.P

That is where you miss the point.

The emphasis is using FOSS on desktops for education and learning, and
not depending on others. Most distro CDs/DVDs have their own manuals
which you can browse. Need to learn to think "positively" and stand on
your own legs and not depend on teachers, the college, society, for
each and everything.

> > Can you tell me how many colleges in India have these, today? Now, we
> > are talking numbers.
>
> If you don't know, IITM has similar facility. Of course ppl are not
> required to have laptops, assignments are emailed, announcements made
> to email and online.. Wireless access is not ubiquitous, though.

That is why I said, "Now, we are talking numbers", meaning, we can count them.
And that is "one" out of how many engineering institutions in this country?

Most GNU/Linux systems have mail servers, content management systems
that they can setup for intranet LAN for educational needs.

> I am not experiencing education abroad, by choice. I did not comment
> on their system. You were comparing the two and I simply asked you not
> to.

The emphasis is to see the best from others and see how you can come
up to their competence level. This is what I meant by
"A-T-T-I-T-U-D-E".

>  At least enough to take that example. Do we not have kids
> hanging aroung shopping malls abroad? Why is that excusable, because
> it is phoren?

That is where you miss the point again.

I accept the fact that there are bad things abroad too. But, why do
you always have to be negative?

Why can't you see the positive things abroad, and try to see how you
can improve yourself with it? Again, this is what I meant in my
previous e-mail as "A-T-T-I-T-U-D-E". You just proved the lack of it
:) This is exactly what I see with students in this country.

As an engineer, if you get stuck in one methodology of problem
solving, you backtrack, and try a different approach. I don't see
these engineering students doing this.

For example, a department in one college borrowed a server from
another department to setup their GNU/Linux user mailing list. It was
pretty active! Once, the other department took back the server, they
were very upset. I waited for a month to see if they will find another
solution. They didn't.

I had to tell them explicitly to create a mailing list for their user
group in googlegroups. Why couldn't they backtrack and think that we
can create an alternative mailing list for the group, an alternative
solution to the problem? This is the "lack of attitude".

> Exactly, then we should not crib about our lack of contrib.

That is what I again meant by "lack of attitude". You just keep
proving it again and again!

You should see how you can overcome that difficulty and prove who you
really are. That is where students seem to accept the fact that it is
their fate or plight that they are here, and they are not doing
anything to improve themselves. It only helps in worsening the already
existing digital divide.

Cheers,

SK

Shakthi Kannan

Interesting, comments are also very good - have arguments against it as well.

"Windows does not support the hardware. The hardware supports Windows.
While people complain that Linux does not have complete drivers for
top 3d graphics cards, *neither does Windows*. Windows does not have
full 3d drivers for these cards, Instead, these 3d graphics cards come
with drivers for Windows."

      Vacancy #1: Systems Engineer

Closes on 25/Aug/2007

Job scope:

- Install and provide technical support to end-customers for HPC clusters,
large SMP servers running Linux (usually), or Solaris (occassionally). End
customers are primarily Universities, Polytechnics, Research Institutes and
commercial firms working on cutting edge IT.

- Install FLOSS and commercial applications : including compiling and
optimizing from source code. Normally applications are MPI parallel apps

- Commission InfiniBand networks

- Handle support calls all the way upto resolution. Includes 24x7 calls.

- Provide technical training on Linux, cluster toolkits and usage of 
software
such as compilers, build tools, Sun Grid Engine etc.

Qualifications:

- Very good skills with Linux esp. x86_64, RHEL/FC and Debian/Ubuntu,
including hands on skills compiling apps, kernels, some experience packaging
etc. Some knowledge of Solaris is good to have

- A diploma or degree in IT or Sciences with preferably 1-year experience.

- Preferably, Singapore citizen or ASEAN citizen since some regional travel
(MY, ID, VN, TH) is involved.

- Some experience or interest in fixing small bugs will be a definite plus.

- Preferably, possess a local driving license.

Must be willing to certify for RHCE if not already certified. (Company will
sponsor)

Please contact me by email: anand@novaglobal.com.sg 
<mailto:anand@novaglobal.com.sg> , remember to send your
resumes in either plain text or ODF format.


      Vacancy #2: Software Systems Engineer

Closes on 30/Sep/2007

I have one new vacancy for an Engineer. The skills I am looking for:

The job involves 60% coding - mostly Java EE, Compute and Data Grids, Apache
tomcat/jBoss applications and some scripting (JS/Bash/Python) and 40% 
Systems
work (eg: Clusters, data grids etc) mostly in an academic and research
environment. The OS env is usually Linux, occassionally Solaris.

Must Have:
- Very good research skills - given a problem, go scour the internet, 
work out
experiments and find the answer

- Willing to pick up new technologies quickly

- Very good with Linux OS. Must have > 2 years Linux desktop/server 
experience
(RHEL, Debian)

- Development experience ~ 1year, contribution to OSS projects can be
considered experience too.

Good to have:
- Preferably possess one of : SCJP, RHCE or LPI, If not certified, must be
willing to certify within a year

- Some understanding of large scale Java systems (eg: jBoss, Websphere etc)
and Grid computing will be great.

- Some exposure to (Open)Solaris.

I am open to hiring fresh graduates if you have enough knowledge and skills.

You can view my company's website at http://www.novaglobal.com.sg/ and find
out the types of projects we are doing.

Please send resumes in either text or openoffice 2.x format to
anand@novaglobal.com.sg <mailto:anand@novaglobal.com.sg>

Compensation will be commensurate with knowledge and skills. We follow 
the variable salary scheme, so there is a good opportunity to earn large 
bonuses at the year end.


      Interview Process: Only for technical positions

After shortlisting your resume, you will be required to attend two 
interviews.

One hands-on project will be assigned as part of the interview process. 
You can return to your home and complete the project in about a week (or 
time estimated during the interview). Since many of our projects involve 
Linux and Open Source software, you can draw resources from the Internet 
to complete the project. A post-project review will decide the hiring 
decision.

From prem at songbirdtech.com  Tue Aug 21 12:24:41 2007
From: prem at songbirdtech.com (Prem Kurian Philip)
Date: Tue Aug 21 12:24:48 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] RE: Linux Hardware Support Better Than Windows
Message-ID: <50535.61.247.255.57.1187679281.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>

>"Windows does not support the hardware. The hardware supports Windows.
>While people complain that Linux does not have complete drivers for
>top 3d graphics cards, *neither does Windows*. Windows does not have
>full 3d drivers for these cards, Instead, these 3d graphics cards come
>with drivers for Windows."

>http://changelog.complete.org/posts/644-Linux-Hardware-Support-Better-Than-Windows.html

I think the summary is a bit misleading. The author is talking about an
instance when he had to change the motherboard on his computer when he
already had Linux and Windows XP installed on it.

He changed the motherboard to find that Linux was able to recognize most
of the hardware without any issues (as all the hardware modules were
already available in the Linux kernel) while in the case of Windows XP, he
had to install the drivers manually for each new device.

PK

Subject: [Ilugc] RE: Linux Hardware Support Better Than Windows
Message-ID: <50661.61.247.255.57.1187680317.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>

>http://changelog.complete.org/posts/644-Linux-Hardware-Support-Better-Than-Windows.html

One of the comments to the article above refers to the problem a user
would face if any the devices are not natively supported in the Linux
kernel. This comment also included this interesting link to an article by
Shuttleworth which further clarifies this point:
http://www.markshuttleworth.com/archives/76

I think Shuttleworth captures the problem of device support on Linux quite
nicely in this post. Device support and quality of device support on Linux
is really a function of the market reach of Linux.

The reason Windows does not ship with drivers for *ALL* supported devices
is because:

a) The device manufacturers ship driver CDs on the disks which accompany
the devices.

b) Pretty much any device out there already has drivers for Windows. We
are talking about so many drivers that the drivers alone will fill up many
CDs.

c) Binary drivers are supported on Windows.

d) OEMs load Windows onto PCs.

I know I got flamed for saying this earlier, but frankly I don't care.
This is the truth.

Regards,
PK

From shakthimaan at gmail.com  Tue Aug 21 13:20:57 2007
From: shakthimaan at gmail.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Tue Aug 21 13:21:08 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] RE: Linux Hardware Support Better Than Windows
In-Reply-To: <50661.61.247.255.57.1187680317.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>
References: <50661.61.247.255.57.1187680317.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>
Message-ID: <d16b1c80708210050m2bfbfa9bm6e3e3b7dfc9702ed@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,

On 8/21/07, Prem Kurian Philip <prem@songbirdtech.com> wrote:
> a) The device manufacturers ship driver CDs on the disks which accompany
> the devices.

They have to write their own drivers for each release of window$,
which is a PITA. They have to work with micro$oft everytime to do
that, which is again a PITA.

Basically, the device manufacturers sign an NDA with micro$oft not to
release any internal information. So, everything is internal. End
result is that end users are only made to think that the product looks
like it works, but, you don't get to see what really doesn't work or
the dirty unresolved work-arounds that go inside. Only developers know
what really doesn't work, and that is not included in the product
marketing :)

The result is that there can be crappy products in the market, that
may not follow any standard, unfortunately.

> b) Pretty much any device out there already has drivers for Windows. We
> are talking about so many drivers that the drivers alone will fill up many
> CDs.

True.

On 8/21/07, Sankarshan Mukhopadhyay <sankarshan.mukhopadhyay@gmail.com> wrote:
> So, what are the factors that prevents similar situation happening for
> Linux ?

We expect hardware vendors to release their datasheets. But, if they
have a crappy product, they get to work with micro$oft, so they don't
release the information to the public, and still make money.
Otherwise, it makes their bugs visible to the public, it may affect
their stock-holders, investors and business, in general.

They also fear that their product might be replicated by somebody else
if they release their hardware data-sheets.

Distros do have some proprietary binary drivers.

Just like a Free Software revolution, there needs to be a Free
Hardware revolution.

Regards,

SK

-- 
Shakthi Kannan
http://www.shakthimaan.com
From prem at songbirdtech.com  Tue Aug 21 13:30:02 2007
From: prem at songbirdtech.com (Prem Kurian Philip)
Date: Tue Aug 21 13:30:08 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: RE: Linux Hardware Support Better Than Windows
Message-ID: <51167.61.247.255.57.1187683202.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>

Sankarshan Mukhopadhyay wrote:

>> b) Pretty much any device out there already has drivers for Windows. We
>> are talking about so many drivers that the drivers alone will fill up many
>> CDs.

>So, what are the factors that prevents similar situation happening for
>Linux ?

The lack of market reach of Linux.

Please read:
http://www.markshuttleworth.com/archives/76

When Linux has more than 5 or 10% of the market, the hardware manufactures
will pay it more attention and be willing to release their drivers more
readily. As it stands, Linux has less than 3% market reach and those
manufacturers who release drivers willingly for Linux are the exception
and not the norm.

Right now, we do have some manufacturers who release their drivers under
GPL, but again, that is not the norm. Actually, a lot of hardware
manufacturers are not even willing to release the specs for their
hardware.

Perhaps when Linux has 20% to 30% market reach, hardware manufacturers may
even be willing to release their driver source files under the GPL.

Regards,
PK

	<d16b1c80708210050m2bfbfa9bm6e3e3b7dfc9702ed@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <200708211444.17336.mrugeshkarnik@gmail.com>

On Tuesday 21 Aug 2007 13:20:57 Shakthi Kannan wrote:
> Distros do have some proprietary binary drivers.

The Linux kernel developers have a policy of not allowing non-GPL'd drivers to 
make it into the kernel. Whether its non-GPL'd or non-free, I'm not sure.

Take nvidia's drivers for example. The kernel module itself is distributed in 
the form of the source code. I notice this because it has to be recompiled on 
Gentoo, everytime I change the kernel. `Binary' distros distribute the debs 
or rpms for these precompiled modules. Obviously, they're compiled by making 
sure that they work properly with the stock distribution kernel. The OpenGL 
libraries and all, however, are closed source.

From prem at songbirdtech.com  Tue Aug 21 19:48:08 2007
From: prem at songbirdtech.com (Prem Kurian Philip)
Date: Tue Aug 21 19:48:14 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Re: RE: Linux Hardware Support Better Than Windows
Message-ID: <54236.61.247.255.57.1187705888.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>

>> a) The device manufacturers ship driver CDs on the disks which accompany
>> the devices.

>They have to write their own drivers for each release of window$,
>which is a PITA. They have to work with micro$oft everytime to do
>that, which is again a PITA.

Actually, there is more work involved in maintaining a Linux driver than
there is maintaining a driver for windows because the windows driver API
is pretty stable. This API hardly ever varies between service pack
releases, while on Linux the kernel ABI is not stable as Linux kernel
developers believe that stabilizing this API will mean reducing their
freedom to improve the API later..

Windows drivers don't have to be updated every single time there is a
service pack update. On occasion, the service pack update may drastically
change the driver interface, only then is the user required to change the
windows driver.

On Linux, you need to recompile the driver when you update even point
release of the kernel, which is why Novell has the Partner Linux Driver
Process.
http://www.linux-watch.com/news/NS5423433687.html


>Basically, the device manufacturers sign an NDA with micro$oft not to
>release any internal information. So, everything is internal.

You can develop hardware drivers for windows without signing a single NDA
with MS. The driver development kit is available for free download and the
API is nicely documented.

http://www.microsoft.com/whdc/driver/wdf/wdfbook.mspx
http://www.microsoft.com/whdc/DevTools/ddk/default.mspx

If you need your driver to be windows certified, then you need to go back
to MS.

>End result is that end users are only made to think that the product looks
>like it works, but, you don't get to see what really doesn't work or
>the dirty unresolved work-arounds that go inside. Only developers know
>what really doesn't work, and that is not included in the product
>marketing :)

I think it is a little unfair to say that the only reason source is not
released is because the developers want to hide their dirty code. There
are so many other reasons why companies may choose to close the source
code to their drivers - proprietary algorithms implemented in the driver
is just one of those reasons.

Regards,
PK
From knura at yahoo.com  Tue Aug 21 19:48:53 2007
From: knura at yahoo.com (Arun Khan)
Date: Tue Aug 21 19:49:10 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] squid proxy and doze dhcp
In-Reply-To: <39589D3F-6448-4DA0-BA81-606D4BB37FE2@thenilgiris.com>
References: <39589D3F-6448-4DA0-BA81-606D4BB37FE2@thenilgiris.com>
Message-ID: <200708211948.53317.knura@yahoo.com>

On Tuesday 21 August 2007 19:05, Kenneth Gonsalves wrote:
>
> doze dhcp server with ip 192.168.1.2 with thin clients in the ip
> range of 192.168.1.4 - 25. Ubuntu server with two ethernet cards:
> eth0 - ip 192.168.1.100 connected to a bsnl modem/router ip address
> 192.168.1.1
> eth1 - ip 192.168.1.126 connected to the lan (doze dhcp lan)
> gateway of eth0 is set as 192.168.1.1
> gateway of eth1 is set as the eth0 ip - 192.168.1.100

An ascii depiction of your network would help - like so:

                     192.168.1.x
BSNL -----------------------------------------------
        |     |           \  ..  \  ....  \
        UbuntuSrvr       Windows  Thin clients

If the above is your topology then your Windows and Thin clients can by 
pass your proxy server.

Suggest you implement the following:

                     192.168.1.x
BSNL ----        --------------------------------------
        |        |           \  ..  \  ....  \
        Ubuntu_Srvr       Windows  Thin clients

Put the BSNL modem/router and Ubuntu eth0 on a 192.168.0.x network.  
Configure SQUID with Internet iface eth0 and LAN iface eth1.

IMO, putting multiple NICs on the same network makes sense when you want 
to increase network thru put.  For SQUID it is a no no.

> I have squid proxy server running on the linux machine.
>
> When eth1 is not connected to the lan, internet works and i am able
> to ping 192.168.1.1 from the linux machine

> when eth1 is connected to the lan, i can ping the doze machine from
> the linux machine and from the doze machine can ping both eth0 and
> eth1. But from the linux machine i cannot ping the modem -
> 192.168.1.1. From the doze machine, squid reports inability to
> connect to the internet.

Follow suggested topology and avoid unnecessary routing headaches.

HTH
-- Arun Khan

On Tue, 21 Aug 2007, Kenneth Gonsalves wrote:

> doze dhcp server with ip 192.168.1.2 with thin clients in the ip  
> range of 192.168.1.4 - 25. Ubuntu server with two ethernet cards:
> eth0 - ip 192.168.1.100 connected to a bsnl modem/router ip address  
> 192.168.1.1
> eth1 - ip 192.168.1.126 connected to the lan (doze dhcp lan)
> gateway of eth0 is set as 192.168.1.1
> gateway of eth1 is set as the eth0 ip - 192.168.1.100

All interfaces are in the same network and routing will be bit
confusing. So to simplify the routing, set eth1 to 192.168.2.100 and
client address as 2.4 - 25.

Bye :)
-- 
Bharathi S


From prem at songbirdtech.com  Tue Aug 21 19:57:59 2007
From: prem at songbirdtech.com (Prem Kurian Philip)
Date: Tue Aug 21 19:58:08 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Re: RE: Linux Hardware Support Better Than Windows
Message-ID: <54272.61.247.255.57.1187706479.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>

>> Distros do have some proprietary binary drivers.

>The Linux kernel developers have a policy of not allowing non-GPL'd
drivers >to make it into the kernel. Whether its non-GPL'd or non-free,
I'm not sure.

>Take nvidia's drivers for example. The kernel module itself is
distributed in
>the form of the source code. I notice this because it has to be
recompiled on
>Gentoo, everytime I change the kernel. `Binary' distros distribute the debs
>or rpms for these precompiled modules. Obviously, they're compiled by making
>sure that they work properly with the stock distribution kernel. The OpenGL
>libraries and all, however, are closed source.

The Nvidia driver (and so also the ATI driver) comes in two parts. The
binary blob which holds the actual code of the driver, and several thin
kernel module interface source files - one each for different point
releases of the Linux kernel.

When you install the driver, the kernel module interface corresponding to
your kernel's version will be compiled and installed - and this kernel
module will in turn load the binary module and forward requests to it.

That is the kernel source file is actually a sort of an interface layer
between the Linux kernel and the binary blob which constitutes the actual
driver. This will most likely introduce some sort of performance penalty
on the use of these drivers on Linux, but I am not sure.

One point though - Nvidia (and I think ATI too) ship with a bunch of
pre-compiled kernel module interfaces for various stock distributions of
Linux kernel. So if you are using one of those stock kernels, the Nvidia
driver installer won't compile the kernel source file.

regards,
PK

From prem at songbirdtech.com  Wed Aug 22 10:57:23 2007
From: prem at songbirdtech.com (Prem Kurian Philip)
Date: Wed Aug 22 10:57:36 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Re: Re: Re: Re: RE: Linux Hardware Support Better Than
	Windows
Message-ID: <49552.61.247.255.57.1187760443.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>

Shakthi Kannan wrote:

>> Windows drivers don't have to be updated every single time there is a
>> service pack update.

>For an end-user. For a developer/tester, prior to releasing the above,
>its a PITA.

I am referring to the developer here. The developer will very rarely have
to change the driver or even recompile it for service pack updates.

That is the same binary driver can be used across service packs, for the
most part. So end-users will rarely have to worry about loading new
drivers.

When XP service pack 2 was released, MS had implemented hardware support
for the data execution prevention (DEP) on some chips which includes this
DEP feature. This required changes in the driver architecture and
therefore some drivers had to be modified.

However, for the most part, when you install service packs, you will
rarely have to change the driver.

>> The driver development kit is available for free download and the
>> API is nicely documented.

>On the assumption that what beneath the API work fine. When they don't
>(most of the time) it is a PITA.

Are you stating this from previous personal experience developing drivers
for Windows or based on the general assumption that anything from MS must
be bad?

It is one thing to criticize MS for its screw ups (and there have been
many), but it is yet another thing to heap criticism just because the
recipient happens to be MS.

I am no fan of MS, but there are things we can learn from it.

But anyway, my point wasn't about MS. My point was about the reason for
the wide availability of windows drivers for hardware when Linux drivers
are more difficult to find.

MS is not holding a gun to the head of the hardware manufacturers to force
them to release drivers for their hardware. These OEMs release the drivers
for windows willingly because they want their hardware to be used by
windows users who constitute the majority.

OEMs are far less keen to release drivers for Linux is because they may
have done a cost-benefit analysis of releasing drivers for Linux and have
obviously come to the conclusion that the slight increase in sales that
they would receive by making their hardware available for use by
Linux-only users is not enough to offset the investment in driver
development.

It is decision driven by business and not technical considerations.

If the number of Linux reaches a critical mass, you can bet that these
OEMs will be falling over each other to release drivers for Linux so as to
not to lose out on sales.

Regards,
PK

The performance of Nvidia cards on Linux does lag behind that on windows:
