To go directly to the benchmarks:
http://www.phoronix.com/scan.php?page=article&item=781&num=3

I am not saying that the reason for the lag is most certainly the
additional kernel interface module required on Linux as a layer between
the kernel and the binary blob which is the actual Nvidia driver, but I
think it may be one of the reasons.

	Than Windows
In-Reply-To: <49552.61.247.255.57.1187760443.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>
	(Prem Kurian Philip's message of "Wed\,
	22 Aug 2007 10\:57\:23 +0530 \(IST\)")
References: <49552.61.247.255.57.1187760443.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>
Message-ID: <866437tzwa.fsf@lark.home>

"Prem Kurian Philip" <prem@songbirdtech.com> writes:
> If the number of Linux reaches a critical mass, you can bet that
> these OEMs will be falling over each other to release drivers
> for Linux so as to not to lose out on sales.

Even if gnu/linux becomes a monopoly on the desktop market., the
linux-kernel wont have a stable driver api. Reason being it is
simply not practical. And., the hardware-vendors wont be able to
match up with the kernel-developers in releasing drivers for every
version of the linux-kernel.

The preferred way of distributing drivers for the Linux kernel is
to publish the driver source under the GPL or provide the specs
for the hardware so that a Free software implementation can be
written.

--

Hi all,
         I was playing/trying around with the chennai mirror as its
listed as the only archive mirror from India & came to following
conclusions/observations. I'm sure a part of this I also put up
sometime back.  :-

1. https://launchpad.net/ubuntu/+archivemirrors :- This lists the IITM
mirror as atleast a week back. Is this true? I find it hard to believe
that we are that back. Of course with 3 distributions there is quite a
bit of syncing to do everyday & I dunno how the priorities are set up.
As a ubuntu user so of course would be biased in looking after that.

2. First of all its cool, just great that you guys have rsync
happening. Now, while  I was playing around with rsync & decided to
give an another archive mirror just to see how rsync behaves with both
of them :-

First up just browsing one of  the mirrors in Europe

 rsync mirror.etf.bg.ac.yu::

I have.

Freedom" contest for University students in India.

Here is what the website has to say,

    Sixty years ago, just as India awoke to freedom,
we call upon the young minds of India to awake to the
clarion call of Open Source. The Open Source movement
is emerging as the new new world order making a
sweeping impact in the technology sector across the
world. Today, Open Source products such as Apache Web
Server, Open Office and Linux have dwarfed several
proprietary software corporations.

    Sun Microsystems, a front-runner in professionally
backing Open Source and one of the largest
contributors to this movement, takes this opportunity
to invite the young, dynamic academic community of
India to come and become a part of the exciting Open
Source wave. We encourage you all to embrace the Open
Source technologies with open hands and help take
these communities to greater heights.

    With this vision, Sun Microsystems is happy to
announce the Code For Freedom contest where students
across India contribute to the technologies that are
empowering the participation age. Participating in
this contest will provide you with precious industry
experience while still learning in college. And there
is more. We in turn reward you for your valuable
contribution in taking the first steps towards the
open source movement.

    Come. Be a part of this phenomenon called, Open
Source.


Are you contributing yet?

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Thu Aug 23 10:08:27 2007
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Thu Aug 23 09:59:28 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] [LJ] Tech Tip
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0708231003490.663-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Linux Journal Tech Tip: Automatic Login with MySQL

This tip comes from Sirgey in Ontario, Canada:

When running non-interactive MySQL commands one may submit MySQL
credentials on the command line, e.g.:

mysql --password=secret --user=username database_name < query.sql

This approach has two drawbacks. First, it is not secure. Second, if
you have many scripts with embedded passwords you will have to take
care of all of them when the time comes to change your password. A
better option is to use a special option file to store login
information. At start up, all MySQL programs read from one or more
global option files, and lastly from the file called .my.cnf in the
user's home directory, if such file exists. All option files have the
same format which consists of a section name followed by options. All
valid command line arguments can be specified in the option file. For
example to enable automatic login your .my.cnf file should look like
this:

# the following section will be read by *all* client programs
[client]
user=username
password=secret
database=database_name

Of course, when creating this file make sure it is only user readable!
Now you can run the batch query with a more simple command which is
suitable for non-interactive jobs, e.g., scheduled with crontab:

mysql < query.sql

And most certainly you can now launch an interactive session with this
compact command:

   mysql

If you need to connect to a different databases or use another user
names it is always possible to override the settings of the option
file on the command line.

Another advantage of using user's option file is that it is very easy
to create an ad-hoc MySQL clients that can be automatically
initialized with user's credentials and other private settings. Here's
how you can do it in Python with the help of the standard module
ConfigParser:

import  ConfigParser
config = ConfigParser.ConfigParser()
# read ~/.my.cnf if it exists but don't raise error if it doesn't
config.read(['site.cfg', os.path.expanduser('~/.my.cnf')])
if config.has_section("client"):
  # got options for MySQL clients
  if config.has_option("client", "password"):
    # got default password
    pass = config.get("client", "password")

From prem at songbirdtech.com  Thu Aug 23 11:16:03 2007
From: prem at songbirdtech.com (Prem Kurian Philip)
Date: Thu Aug 23 11:16:11 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Re: Re: Re: Re: Re: RE: Linux Hardware Support Better
 Than Windows
Message-ID: <49445.61.247.255.57.1187847963.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>

>> If the number of Linux reaches a critical mass, you can bet that
>> these OEMs will be falling over each other to release drivers
>> for Linux so as to not to lose out on sales.

>Even if gnu/linux becomes a monopoly on the desktop market., the
>linux-kernel wont have a stable driver api. Reason being it is
>simply not practical.

Why do you think it won't be practical?

If you want to know how practical (or not) the current approach is, please
do read up on the the kind of trouble enterprise linux vendors are facing
when it comes to managing the driver modules, please see:
http://www.kroah.com/log/linux/enterprise_kernel_future.html

> And., the hardware-vendors wont be able to
>match up with the kernel-developers in releasing drivers for every
>version of the linux-kernel.

If the driver API is stable, the OEMs will need to release drivers only
occasionally, and not as often as they have to do now. Which means that
they will be able to maintain the drivers themselves without requiring
external developers to write drivers for their hardware.

>The preferred way of distributing drivers for the Linux kernel is
>to publish the driver source under the GPL or provide the specs
>for the hardware so that a Free software implementation can be
>written.

That would be the *ideal* case, but life is far from ideal.

Regards,

"Prem Kurian Philip" <prem@songbirdtech.com> writes:
> If the driver API is stable, the OEMs will need to release
> drivers only occasionally, and not as often as they have to do
> now. Which means that they will be able to maintain the drivers
> themselves without requiring external developers to write
> drivers for their hardware.

No software is ever 100% bug-free. Every piece of software goes
through constant refactoring to make it better. So., if the OEM
guys release at such large intervals it means one of the two.,

     (1) Their driver code is perfect and does not need
     refactoring.

     (2) They dont care (not a business issue) that their code is
     performing poorly or has bugs.

I really dont think it is (1). So., it makes a lot of sense to
make the driver source available to the community so that the
community and other interested third party will take care of the
issues.

>>The preferred way of distributing drivers for the Linux kernel
>>is to publish the driver source under the GPL or provide the
>>specs for the hardware so that a Free software implementation
>>can be written.
>
> That would be the *ideal* case, but life is far from ideal.

Yes., and we cannot deny that a lot of hardware vendors are moving
to this model. So maybe soon life will indeed become ideal :)

From rautelap at gmail.com  Thu Aug 23 12:56:05 2007
From: rautelap at gmail.com (pradeep singh rautela)
Date: Thu Aug 23 12:56:14 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Re: Re: Re: Re: Re: RE: Linux Hardware Support Better
	Than Windows

On 8/23/07, Prem Kurian Philip <prem@songbirdtech.com> wrote:
[...]
>
> Why do you think it won't be practical?
>
> If you want to know how practical (or not) the current approach is, please
> do read up on the the kind of trouble enterprise linux vendors are facing
> when it comes to managing the driver modules, please see:
> http://www.kroah.com/log/linux/enterprise_kernel_future.html

please see this too http://kernelslacker.livejournal.com/82610.html .

>
> If the driver API is stable, the OEMs will need to release drivers only
> occasionally, and not as often as they have to do now. Which means that
> they will be able to maintain the drivers themselves without requiring
> external developers to write drivers for their hardware.

API usually stays stable. Fortunately and unfortunately (whatever you
may call it), the in kernel API which matters to the hardware
manufacturers remains stable mostly. Only way it breaks is when a
major subsystem gets a rework to fix some xyz regression. Aliter still
then the API is kept intact for legacy drivers like ones OEM may be
using. The deprecated API may vanish but not so soon. There is a
certain time frame given. Linux kernel is fast, very fast moving
software. Terminally dead API get rewritten or removed entirely.
Porting a driver across API changes[and not kernels i mean here] is
not very difficult.
But as Joe rightly said the best way to get over this is to publish a
driver as a GPLed code and get it merged in the official kernel
tree(another difficult task).

If hardware manufacturers do not care about their drivers, its their
headache IMO. They should be ready to update the drivers like any
other software i think. And if they do not want to, better get it
included in the kernel tree.

My 2 cents.

thanks
--psr

>>Porting a driver across API changes[and not kernels i mean here] is
>>not very difficult.

>> http://www.kroah.com/log/linux/enterprise_kernel_future.html

And the link you posted:
>please see this too http://kernelslacker.livejournal.com/82610.html .

The links I have posted and the one you posted both contradict your
statement that porting a driver across API changes is not very difficult.

Actually, it is *very* time consuming, tedious and difficult to maintain
the modules across so many different kernel releases. Please read those
links again.

The job of backporting changes from different upstream kernel releases to
various kernel modules literally takes months and is currently only
happening because Novell, Redhat etc have a lot of paid staff working on
this.

>If hardware manufacturers do not care about their drivers, its their
>headache IMO.

Are you sure? Ultimately all it means is that Linux users don't get to use
the latest and greatest hardware. As for the OEMs, we (Linux users) are
such a minuscule percentage of the market, they couldn't care less if we
didn't buy their hardware.

I don't want to repeat myself, but I have addressed this point earlier in
the thread. Market reach is everything when it comes to Linux user's
ability to get hardware manufacturers to provide drivers.

Regards,
PK

From prem at songbirdtech.com  Thu Aug 23 14:07:55 2007
From: prem at songbirdtech.com (Prem Kurian Philip)
Date: Thu Aug 23 14:08:15 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Re: Re: Re: Re: Re: Re: RE: Linux Hardware Support
 Better Than Windows
Message-ID: <51428.61.247.255.57.1187858275.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>

pradeep singh rautela wrote:

>> Its actually quite interesting that the quality checking process
>> (peer review) in an Open Source project is more stringent than in
>> any other proprietary software company :D

>yes, thats one of the reason you ll find occasional flamewars between
>corporate kernel developers and kernel hackers. I wonder when will it
>take for whole world to realize that open source development model is
>a far superior development model than any closed source ones.

I agree. Open source is a superior model of development. I think the world
already realizes that to some extent.

However, the problem with the driver situation in Linux is not a problem
of the development model, but rather of architecture.

The Linux kernel architecture does not include a driver ABI - and that was
a deliberate decision to force companies to release the source for the
drivers.. actually, Linus did relent somewhat and released some support in
the kernel module architecture to allow for the kernel module interfaces
to be called from non-GPLed modules.

http://ussg.iu.edu/hypermail/linux/kernel/0110.2/0369.html

However, as a side effect of this, we have fewer hardware drivers.

Some interesting notes to this:
http://ussg.iu.edu/hypermail/linux/kernel/0110.2/0447.html
http://ussg.iu.edu/hypermail/linux/kernel/0110.2/0457.html

Regards,
PK

On 8/24/07, Prashanth <munichlinux@gmail.com> wrote:
>
> hi,
>
>         I want to take a automatic incremental mysql backup whenever there
> is a insert or update happening to the database but i dont like to
> schedule the process(something like every hour or day). Is there any
> tool or script through which i can achieve this?
>

use one way replication. and run a shell script to back it up every 1 hour
or so if you need hard backup... If it is a production system, it is better
to use replication. Please check mysql documentation for details.

Subject: [Ilugc] Mysql backup
In-Reply-To: <1f869bdd0708232218w3b04749ep46e2c14d6be18bb4@mail.gmail.com>

On 8/24/07, Prashanth <munichlinux@gmail.com> wrote:
> On 8/24/07, PV Sundarram <pvsundarram@gmail.com> wrote:
> > hi
> >
> >
> >
> > use one way replication. and run a shell script to back it up every 1 hour
> > or so if you need hard backup
>
> I dont want to schedule the process like you said everyone hour there
> might be a loss of data if the server crashes between that.
>
> ... If it is a production system, it is better
> > to use replication.
>
> I have one slice so i can't do replication too.  Sorry i forgot to
> mention this.

If you are ready for performance trade-off, enable logging in mysql.
Write a script to parse the log file every minute and pass on the sqls
(insert, update, delete and which sql you like) to different mysql
server on same machine or mysql server on different machine.

Another possible work around is to mirror the data directory using
rsync command periodically. I'm not sure if this would suit the
purpose.
--

Bhuvaneswaran A
www.livecipher.com

---------Posting on behalf of Rahul Chopra, Editor, Linux For You----------

Hi all,

Niraj's post represents the confusion (and frustration) that the team was 
undergoing when they were trying to resolve customer complaints, and yet 
were faced with instructions ranging from--'keep this discussion off the 
list' to 'take action or else...'.

The latest issue of LFY (Debian special) has experienced some major problems 
w.r.t. delivery. We have pulled up the courier agency (Professional 
Couriers) and may shift back to the Indian postal system where the magazines 
and disks were sent separately--an Indianised strategy that seemingly 
results in least complaints.

However, we do apologise to:

1. Kenneth, for calling him... However, we do plead him to take us as part 
of the community world, and not treat us as some evil force :-)

2. The members of this LUG who had requested us to not to post any messages 
w.r.t. that complaint. We tried, but could not hold back, since it was clear 
that taking discussions offline might be interpreted as 'LFY not interested 
in their customers' by the rest.

3. Most importantly, our subscribers--who've faced issues since we've been 
experimenting with courier agencies. We'll surely correct this asap. In the 
meantime, if ever there's a delay in receipt of copies--please do shoot an 
email to support@efyindia.com and niraj@efyindia.com (he (tries to) build 
relations with the community). You may also mark me a CC at 
lfyedit@efyindia.com.

May the source remain with us too, through these testing times...

Yours truly,
Rahul Chopra

From mail-lists at karan.org  Fri Aug 24 14:24:15 2007
From: mail-lists at karan.org (Karanbir Singh)
Date: Fri Aug 24 14:23:22 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Mysql backup
In-Reply-To: <1f869bdd0708232203t1e15d90ew35c37052e29d3ccf@mail.gmail.com>
References: <1f869bdd0708232203t1e15d90ew35c37052e29d3ccf@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <46CE9CB7.9090507@karan.org>

Prashanth wrote:
> hi,
> 
>  	I want to take a automatic incremental mysql backup whenever there
> is a insert or update happening to the database but i dont like to
> schedule the process(something like every hour or day). Is there any
> tool or script through which i can achieve this?
> 

as Bhuvaneswaran already said, your best option is to enable mysql's
binlog. What size / type db are you running ? its usually a good idea to
put the binlogs on a different drive / spindleset from the main db
storage. Firstly, it increases data reliability but more importantly (
to me anyway ) it reduces the performance degradation you are likely to
see by enabling binlogs

- KB

Karanbir Singh : http://www.karan.org/ : 2522219@icq

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Fri Aug 24 18:49:24 2007
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Fri Aug 24 18:40:11 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] FYI: India throws M$ OOXML out of the Window
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0708241840480.2374-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Posted by Vinayak Hegde at GII-India

Link: http://economictimes.indiatimes.com/Infotech/Software/
India_throws_Microsoft_open_format_out_of_the_window/articleshow/2305780.cms
(url has wrapped)

NEW DELHI: India on Thursday gave Microsoft a thumbs-down in the war
of standards for office documents. In a tense meeting at Delhi's Manak
Bhawan, the 21-member technical committee decided that India will vote
a 'no' against Microsoft's Open Office Extensible Mark Up Language
(OOXML) standard at the International Standards Organisation (ISO) in
Geneva on September 2.

"We unanimously agree on the disapproval of OOXML with comments. The
same will be submitted to ISO," National Informatics Centre head and
BIS technical committee chairperson Nita Verma said after a marathon
meeting that lasted over six hours. There was no need for a voting as
only Infosys Technologies and CSI supported Microsoft.

The Open Document Format (ODF) alliance, enjoying widespread support
from academia and corporates like Oracle, IBM, Red Hat, Sun
Microsystems, Google, were in a jubilant mood having succeeded in
stalling OOXML from being accepted as a standard in India.

Microsoft said it respect's the government's decision. "There were
only three options `Yes', `No' and `Abstain' to be taken and we
respect the government's decision," Microsoft's legal affairs head
Rakesh Bakshi said. He, however, added that India's 'No' vote will
become a 'Yes' if Microsoft is able to resolve all technical issues
with OOXML before the ballot resolution committee of ISO.

Prof DB Phatak of IIT Mumbai, who was instrumental in conducting the
meetings, looked relieved after being flooded with calls from both
camps over the week.

Speaking to ET outside the BIS premises, the Microsoft camp complained
that when ODF was being standardised by ISO, they did not oppose it
and now the ODF camp refused to return the favour. ODF supporters said
they would have no problems with OOXML if all the 200 technical issues
were taken care of.

Amongst hectic lobbying from both camps, the US government on Thursday
said that it will abstain from voting. China has already voted a 'No'
against Microsoft, while Malaysia, Denmark and Switzerland are
supporting the software major.

A global alliance of Sun-IBM, Oracle, Google, Red Hat have ganged up
against Microsoft which is being supported by Apple, Quark, Accenture
and Novell. 

On Indian soil, Infosys, HCL, Skelta, Sonata Software and Sify have
come out in support of Microsoft.

September 2 is the last date to submit the vote with comments to ISO.
About 123 counties are participating in the vote. Votes from most are
still to come. Canada, Czech Republic, Iran, Japan, Libya, Cuba, New
Zealand, UK are likely to back the IBM-Sun's ODF Alliance. On the
other hand, Belgium, Finland, Italy, Spain, Brazil, Singapore, Korea,
France and Australia are likely to abstain from voting.

Bye :)
--
Bharathi S

You can do browsing from command line using lynx/links/w3m. OR If
you want to use GUI, then ssh with "Enables X11 forwarding (-X, read
man ssh)" and run the firefox from command line of remote pc.

From raamanp at yahoo.co.in  Sat Aug 25 15:41:41 2007
From: raamanp at yahoo.co.in (Raman.P)
Date: Sat Aug 25 15:42:11 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Remote Desktop sharing
In-Reply-To: <15659.203.212.230.148.1188034041.squirrel@203.212.230.148>
Message-ID: <815492.79961.qm@web7910.mail.in.yahoo.com>


--- Bharathi Subramanian <sbharathi@MidasComm.com> wrote:

> Padhu Indianathann said:
> 
> > (RHEL 4). Presently i use ssh. But it is in command prompt. I
> could
> > not make an browsing from remote computer.
> 
> You can do browsing from command line using lynx/links/w3m. OR If
> you want to use GUI, then ssh with "Enables X11 forwarding (-X,
> read
> man ssh)" and run the firefox from command line of remote pc.

If you want full desktop like kde,gnome  run
startkde or gnome-session
after connecting through ssh [X11forwarding enabled].

Alternatively, you can use Xnest inside present X to call remote.
xdmcp should be true in gdm/kdm.

Alternatively in runlevel 3, run X -query remote to get remote
display manager login. For this you should set xdmcp enable option to
true in gdm.conf or kdmrc

Loot at XDMCP-HOWTO in tldp.org for more details.

Raman.P

On 26-Aug-07, at 12:28 PM, Suresh Ramasubramanian wrote:

>> On 25-Aug-07, at 3:34 PM, Natarajan V wrote:
>>> For the past few months, I have been facing a funny (and costly)
>>> problem. When I switch on my PC's power supply
>> what do you mean by 'PC's power supply'?
>
> 220V 50 Hz AC (or whatever passes for it, that is supplied by the  
> TNEB)

in that case:
1. It is advisable to have a stabilizer/UPS - if you use raw power,  
everything will blow
2. Check the earthing
3. Check that the line and neutral are not reversed
4. replace the SMS on your CPU

Hi all,

I am facing a similar kind of issue as the irctc.co.in issue on the
list a few days back. But this is more technical. I was trying to
register my HSBC internet banking from hsbc.co.in when I got this
error "SSL Enforcement"

"The browser you are using is currently set at a lower strength of
encryption than is required to access your HSBC Internet Banking
services.

Please click one of the following links below. These links will guide
you to where you can upgrade/download the 128-bit encryption for your
browser.

                                         Netscape         Internet Explorer
"

To let you know, I am using Firefox 2.0.0.6 (With SSL 3 Enabled and
TLS 1.0 enabled and even SSL 2 is tweaked to be enabled) on FC3. I
don't understand in which way is it less secure. I have already put up
this issue with HSBC. I would like to know whether my browser supports
128 bit SSL (I think it can upto 256bit). I have googled and came to
this already existing issue in Korea
(http://www.kanai.net/weblog/archive/2007/01/26/00h53m55s). I think
HSBC uses ActiveX controls. I would like to know the tweak in FF to
help me with this issue. I have already tweaked it to enable SSL 2
(which was disabled because of SSL3). I even tried changing the FF
identity as IE7 but nothing worked. Is the M$ monopoly playing here.
Can any one help me???

Natarajan V <rajanvn@gmail.com> wrote:

> Thanks for the responses. I got my SMPS replaced and it does boot up
> properly now. This is the third SMPS for my PC. At Pammal we get 240V
> 50Hz electricity from TNEB :(.

Get a good UPS - preferably something rated a bit higher - 650 VA or even 1 
kVA

And get a good brand like APC - dont buy cheap random / unknown UPS brands. 
A few hundred rupees extra for a good UPS will save the rest of your 
peripherals

Learnt that the hard way after an earlier PC that had an ATI radeon card in 
it blew .. and that too in Adyar, which has a rather better power situation 
than Pammal thanks to so many politicians and officials living in the area, 
so that the TNEB is a bit more careful about providing good service here.

"Natarajan V" <rajanvn@gmail.com> wrote:


> got an APC UPS and have a Printer cum scanner connected to it.....

Next step - make sure your power strip that you plug into the UPS, and that 
has all your peripherals and your PC plugged into it, is ALSO of good 
quality, ideally with separate switches for each plug point, instead of one 
central switch, and with a line filter built into it.

Oh, and test the power strip sockets for proper earthing, polarity reversal 
etc

Another few hundred rupees on buying a good strip won't go wrong. And it 
will save you a lot of money.

    suresh

> hi,
>
> I have a setup like this:
>
> doze dhcp server with ip 192.168.1.2 with thin clients in the ip
> range of 192.168.1.4 - 25. Ubuntu server with two ethernet cards:
> eth0 - ip 192.168.1.100 connected to a bsnl modem/router ip address
> 192.168.1.1
> eth1 - ip 192.168.1.126 connected to the lan (doze dhcp lan)
> gateway of eth0 is set as 192.168.1.1
> gateway of eth1 is set as the eth0 ip - 192.168.1.100
>
> I have squid proxy server running on the linux machine.
>
> When eth1 is not connected to the lan, internet works and i am able
> to ping 192.168.1.1 from the linux machine
>
> when eth1 is connected to the lan, i can ping the doze machine from
> the linux machine and from the doze machine can ping both eth0 and
> eth1. But from the linux machine i cannot ping the modem -
> 192.168.1.1. From the doze machine, squid reports inability to
> connect to the internet.
>

 Could you please verify the IP addresses you have posted. Given the
current setup, your windows and thin clients will easily bypass the
proxy. You need to break the setup in two subnets. 192.168.1.x talks
to the bsnl router and 192.168.y.z talk to normal lan. And yes do a
google search on 'NAT'.

On Monday 27 August 2007 12:59, Antano Solar wrote:
> I notice a considerable quality difference when playing music in
> linux (debian , ubuntu , suse) and in windows.
> I am using a via chipset.
> Have noticed this in gnome and kde (using alsa and oss ).
>
> I find the quality much superior when playing it in windows.
> Am I missing something ?
> or is it a driver issue .

You have not mentioned the kind of music you play but presume you are 
playing the "same" source files through the same hardware under Windows 
and Linux and under same settings e.g. output levels, equalizer etc.

Nonetheless, this is subjective.  Each of us have different audio and 
visual capabilities.  For example, I can notice the flicker on CRT 
monitors for vert. refresh rates < 70Hz.  Whereas, many of my 
colleagues don't notice the flicker at all even @ 60Hz.

> Kindly let me know , if there is any solution.

Try updating to the latest version of the resp. codec libraries - just a 
thought.

HTH,
-- Arun Khan

From mohan.tux at gmail.com  Mon Aug 27 19:06:36 2007
From: mohan.tux at gmail.com (Mohan Sundaram)
Date: Mon Aug 27 19:07:07 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Bandwidth shaping on two interfaces
In-Reply-To: <5ff65e910708270325o657dc1d3vfad0aca435f1bf4d@mail.gmail.com>
References: <5ff65e910708270325o657dc1d3vfad0aca435f1bf4d@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <46D2D364.2090002@gmail.com>

Prasanna David G wrote:
> Hello all,
> 
> I have a firewall (Debian sarge 2.6.8-1) with 3 interfaces.
> eth1 -> ISP (202...)                                        256 Kbps down /
> 80 Kbps up
> eth0 -> Department 1 (192.168.0.0/24)
> eth2 -> Department 2 (192.168.10.0/24)
> (I use IPtables and squid as an intercepting(transparent) proxy)
> 
> This is what I want to do:
> 
>>From 7.45am - 8.45am and from 4pm to 6pm
> Department 2 should get to use atleast 224 Kbps and Department 1 atleast 32
> Kbps
> 
> Other times,
> Department 1 should get atleast 192 Kbps.
> 
> (of course, any spare bandwidth can be used by any one).
> As of now, my priority is not in classifying bulk/interactive traffic.
> 
> I am a little confused as to what to do.  According to LARTC, qdiscs are for
> only one interface.  Do I have to do ingress policing ? Or IMQ ?
> 
> 
> Please advice me.  As some other people also have to maintain the firewall,
> a not so difficult to understand solution would be very helpful.
> 
> regards,
> Prasanna David
>
You need to use tc or squid pools. tc gives you better control. Squid 
can be used to mark packets (FWMARK or TOS) based on request originator 
address and use the mark in tc for classification into appropriate 
classes. Squid supports tcp_outgoing_tos directive in acl where src 
address cacn be used.

Useful sites are
[1] http://lartc.org
[2] http://www.linux-ip.net
[3] http://www.docum.org.

Mohan
From mohan.tux at gmail.com  Mon Aug 27 19:13:34 2007
From: mohan.tux at gmail.com (Mohan Sundaram)
Date: Mon Aug 27 19:14:08 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Bandwidth shaping on two interfaces
In-Reply-To: <46D2D364.2090002@gmail.com>
References: <5ff65e910708270325o657dc1d3vfad0aca435f1bf4d@mail.gmail.com>
	<46D2D364.2090002@gmail.com>
Message-ID: <46D2D506.20908@vsnl.com>

Mohan Sundaram wrote:
> You need to use tc or squid pools. tc gives you better control. Squid 
> can be used to mark packets (FWMARK or TOS) based on request originator 
> address and use the mark in tc for classification into appropriate 
> classes. Squid supports tcp_outgoing_tos directive in acl where src 
> address cacn be used.
> 
> Useful sites are
> [1] http://lartc.org
> [2] http://www.linux-ip.net
> [3] http://www.docum.org.
> 
> Mohan
> 
Forgot to mention that fwmark is useful only if the m/c running squid is 
also the edge router else use TOS/DSMARK.

Reason: fwmark is part of packet context and does not travel out of the 
box. TOS/DSMARK is part of the packet headers and can be used by 
downstream edge equipment.

Mohan

> Hi people,
> I hope this is not a common question, but I just can't get yum to work.

> think.

You _have_ to use ntlmaps. Once you get ntlmaps running, the proxy
http://localhost:5865 will work fine.

NTLmaps instructions are here:
http://iitmlug.wiki-site.com/index.php/Ntlmaps

From lawgon at thenilgiris.com  Tue Aug 28 11:13:34 2007
From: lawgon at thenilgiris.com (Kenneth Gonsalves)
Date: Tue Aug 28 11:13:59 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Reg MUKT open source festival at Govt Institute of
	Electronics - Hyderabad...
In-Reply-To: <ed2d3c000708270407r50f0d7b5tea47982512274d6b@mail.gmail.com>
References: <ed2d3c000708270407r50f0d7b5tea47982512274d6b@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <98463EA6-C43B-475F-A0CA-A9B20C8499ED@thenilgiris.com>


On 27-Aug-07, at 4:37 PM, ?????????? wrote:

> I could see and appreciate our unity when i heard that ILUGH is
> divided into two groups and practically no support to this festival
> other than the two friends came up to address the crowd. I heard that
> the organiser of mukt approached several people for assistance , some
> responded positively. With many hurdles guys had manage to pull a
> success out of many odds.

this is not a completely accurate. As far as I know, the Hyderabad  
LUG is pretty active - it has an active mailing list and fairly  
regularly has meetings on the last saturday of the month. I have  
attended one of the meetings and it had a good crowd. The speakers  
are funded and they have had some very good speakers at times. Each  
LUG is different, and I do not think that any LUG should comment on  
the internal affairs of LUGs in other cities. Every city has some  
dead LUGs - I think, looking at yahoogroups, there are even several  
so-called LUGs in Chennai also.

NRC-FOSS was approached by the organisers for support and funding,  
but we pointed out that the organisers had not involved the local  
LUG, and that we would like to support activities through the local  
LUG/FSUG as far as possible. The organisers were members of the LUG  
mailing list, and they should have put the proposal on the mailing  
list. If they had not got response, that is another matter. They  
should have at least tried. We asked them to address the mailing  
list, and they got some response, although it was very late in the  
day. Quite a few people were positive about it, and some of them  
participated. If they had done this at the outset, there would have  
been much more impact.

I am replying at length to this, as I feel that people should realise  
that the way to approach a LUG is *not* by privately speaking to  
office bearers, but by joining the mailing list and putting forward  
ideas there. Later arrangements can be done by private mails. So  
spreading something like ILUGH is inactive and didnt support the  
initiative is not good. The mailing list was approached at the last  
minute, when everything was finalised. What do you expect them to do?

I appreciate the good job the organisers have done - but it could  
have been much better if the LUG had been involved from the start. I  
hope at least in future they will do so. Any report of the event in  
the LUG mailing list?

-- 

regards
kg
http://lawgon.livejournal.com
http://nrcfosshelpline.in/web/

>        <script>
>        function EvalSound(soundobj) {
>          var thissound=document.getElementById(soundobj);
>          thissound.Play();
>        }
>        </script>
>
>        <embed src="success.wav" autostart=false width=0 height=0
> id="sound1"
>        enablejavascript="true">
>
>        <form>
>        <input type="button" value="Play Sound" onClick="EvalSound
> ('sound1')">
>        </form>
>
> In konq, it plays on every alternate press of the button. In firefox
> it plays sometimes. If i have another button that runs thissound.Stop
> (), in konq, the play button plays, the stop button stops, so after
> clicking the stop button, the play button will play the sound. If I
> dont use the stop button, it plays on every alternate click of the
> play button.
>
> In firefox the play button plays the sound occasionaly. But on
> clicking the stop button it plays every time
>
> if I do this:
>
> <script>
>        function EvalSound(soundobj) {
>          var thissound=document.getElementById(soundobj);
>          thissound.Play();
>         thissound.Stop();
>        }
>        </script>
>
> In firefox, it plays on every click. In konq it never plays. Any clues?
>
>
> It must be the difference in the locking mechanism of the sound  resource
handled by konqueror and firefox. Sometimes konqueror behaves very
differently if the sound system (arts ) is enabled. Try disabling it , maybe
you will get different results.

because of our own experience with ILUG-C. -- unless, of course, they
are from a recognised (or at least recognizable!) organization.

funds needed.

for future events.

From indianathann at gmail.com  Tue Aug 28 18:14:58 2007
From: indianathann at gmail.com (Padhu Indianathann)
Date: Tue Aug 28 18:15:19 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Power supply from TNEB
Message-ID: <e43212340708280544r65726fd2oe6d56f46ca50595b@mail.gmail.com>

Dear Experts,
                   Voltage regulation is an tedious job. In TNEB ring main
system is used. The distance between Power generation plant and the Load
point will vary from 40 Kms 300 Kms. From generation point to utilization
area  TNEB  maintains various  voltage levels as 11000 volts (11KV), 110KV,
230 KV and 440V 3 phase etc to reduce the Line loss . In minor variation in
High voltage side causes remarkable value in domestic side. In addition to
the above, there are drastically raised demand causes overload of Generators
cause low voltages and frequent power failures. In Hill areas like Ooty,
Kodaikanal, Vallparai etc fault rectification work is tedious.

                     I request you to all to take adequate protection
against surges and power fluctuations. It is quit useful if you make an good
earthing for PC Lines. I request u to buy an metal oxide surge divertors
cost around Rs.150/= per phase. Use good quality UPS. One more thing i
suggest u to take an Insurance against ur domestic or Office equipments. I
saw this in one Private Bank, they took policy against their Office PCs.

N.Padmanathan

From rajanvn at gmail.com  Tue Aug 28 21:11:38 2007
From: rajanvn at gmail.com (Natarajan V)
Date: Tue Aug 28 21:11:52 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] differences between konq and ff in playing sound
In-Reply-To: <6BCA137A-F88C-4091-BD92-67EAE2E147CF@thenilgiris.com>
References: <6BCA137A-F88C-4091-BD92-67EAE2E147CF@thenilgiris.com>
Message-ID: <e977d4310708280841t2a705f77ic640644f5e32974a@mail.gmail.com>

On 8/27/07, Kenneth Gonsalves <lawgon@thenilgiris.com> wrote:
> hi,
>
> I have this code:
>
>        <script>
>        function EvalSound(soundobj) {
>          var thissound=document.getElementById(soundobj);
>          thissound.Play();
>        }
>        </script>
>
>        <embed src="success.wav" autostart=false width=0 height=0
> id="sound1"
>        enablejavascript="true">
>
>        <form>
>        <input type="button" value="Play Sound" onClick="EvalSound
> ('sound1')">
>        </form>
>
> In konq, it plays on every alternate press of the button. In firefox
> it plays sometimes. If i have another button that runs thissound.Stop
> (), in konq, the play button plays, the stop button stops, so after
> clicking the stop button, the play button will play the sound. If I
> dont use the stop button, it plays on every alternate click of the
> play button.
>
> In firefox the play button plays the sound occasionaly. But on
> clicking the stop button it plays every time

Good observation.  I was not able to truly simulate the problem, as my
FF said, it can't recognize embedded WAV files. Anyways, here is my
observation based on your inputs and my little experiments with Konq.

FF tries to play the wave file as if it is a synchronous function
call. This means that FF will execute the next statement after finish
playing the sound file.

Konq. on the other hand invokes an external application (amarok in my
case) to play the sound file and doesnt care if amarok played it or
crashed or whatever. Therefore, after invoking amarok, konq. continues
to execute the next statement.


> if I do this:
>
> <script>
>        function EvalSound(soundobj) {
>          var thissound=document.getElementById(soundobj);
>          thissound.Play();
>         thissound.Stop();
>        }
>        </script>
>
> In firefox, it plays on every click. In konq it never plays. Any clues?


In this case, as said earlier, Konq. asks amarok to play the file,
goes to the next statement and asks amarok to stop playing the music.
This explains why you dont hear anything with Konq. with the above
script, whereas in FF you hear the music.

JavaScript by itself has not yet been standardized across all
browsers. When it comes to newer extensions, the problem is even more
prominent. AFAIK, you might have to code separately for each browser
by adding a delay for Konq. before calling Stop :(


with regards,
Natarajan.

On 8/27/07, Mohan Sundaram <mohan.tux@gmail.com> wrote:
>
> Mohan Sundaram wrote:
> > You need to use tc or squid pools. tc gives you better control. Squid
> > can be used to mark packets (FWMARK or TOS) based on request originator
> > address and use the mark in tc for classification into appropriate
> > classes. Squid supports tcp_outgoing_tos directive in acl where src
> > address cacn be used.
> >
> > Useful sites are
> > [1] http://lartc.org
> > [2] http://www.linux-ip.net
> > [3] http://www.docum.org.
> >
> > Mohan
> >
> Forgot to mention that fwmark is useful only if the m/c running squid is
> also the edge router else use TOS/DSMARK.
>
> Reason: fwmark is part of packet context and does not travel out of the
> box. TOS/DSMARK is part of the packet headers and can be used by
> downstream edge equipment.
>
>
Thanks a lot.  I am looking at the documentation on those sites.

I didn't want to do with squid as, during peak hours - when traffic shaping
becomes necessary - lot of people use instant messengers.  I need to
consider all traffic.

Meanwhile, I was wondering if anyone in this list did face the same problem
as mine - that is shaping outgoing traffic on two interfaces.  It will be
helpful to hear from them.

regards,
Prasanna David

From mohan.tux at gmail.com  Wed Aug 29 09:59:05 2007
From: mohan.tux at gmail.com (Mohan Sundaram)
Date: Wed Aug 29 09:59:27 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Bandwidth shaping on two interfaces
In-Reply-To: <5ff65e910708281037j62c328aqab1e725148ac2f5d@mail.gmail.com>
References: <5ff65e910708270325o657dc1d3vfad0aca435f1bf4d@mail.gmail.com>	<46D2D364.2090002@gmail.com>
	<46D2D506.20908@vsnl.com>
	<5ff65e910708281037j62c328aqab1e725148ac2f5d@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <46D4F611.5030605@gmail.com>

Prasanna David G wrote:
> I didn't want to do with squid as, during peak hours - when traffic shaping
> becomes necessary - lot of people use instant messengers.  I need to
> consider all traffic.
1/ You must use squid to mark traffic as connections from squid will all 
have src ip of that proxy m/c which is what tc sees.
2/ try ipp2p or l7-filter on the outgoing interface to ISP to mark p2p 
and other protocol state/type based packets and then use tc.
3/ I did not notice your q on IMQ. qdiscs for shaping are used for 
outgoing traffic. As a rule, outgoing traffic is shaped and incoming 
policed. It is enough if you use tc on the ISP facing interface for 
outgoing traffic. IMQ is used to shape aggregate of incoming and 
outgoing traffic. Does not work well in most cases except for Indian 
ISPs who sell bandwidth by aggregate on in+out traffic rather than 
symmetric duplex bandwidth like in the US.
4/ In most cases, shaping outgoing is enough unless you've enormous 
downloads happening. Downloads happen using http and thus squid is a 
good means to control. IMHO, you must use a combo of Squid to mark and 
tc to shape traffic on the ISP facing interface. On each LAN facing 
interface apply tc based on dst ip to control downloads outside or 
inclusive of http.
> 
> Meanwhile, I was wondering if anyone in this list did face the same problem
> as mine - that is shaping outgoing traffic on two interfaces.  It will be
> helpful to hear from them.
Pretty common n/w config. Your case has only one ISP facing i/f. It gets 
very tricky when you get 2xISP facing interfaces leading to DGD, 
priorities, load balancing, aggregate shaping etc.


Mohan

a FOSS event, the funding has to be applied for by a recognised body

College etc. In the event of it being virgin territory, then we may  
recognise a group of individuals. Hyderabad is not virgin territory,  
there is an active LUG there and hence we will only fund initiatives  
that involve the LUG - there is an active FSUG also, and initiatives  
through them would also be funded. And, to put it very bluntly, we do  
not appreciate propaganda that the Hyderabad LUG is dead/inactive.

From solar345 at gmail.com  Wed Aug 29 11:52:53 2007
From: solar345 at gmail.com (Antano Solar)
Date: Wed Aug 29 11:53:14 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] [OT] Boot up and USB problems
In-Reply-To: <e977d4310708250304p69c6ea73k6b9ca2839f334326@mail.gmail.com>
References: <e977d4310708250304p69c6ea73k6b9ca2839f334326@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <b2600ec40708282322m22ba46ep14e2c829e12a9226@mail.gmail.com>

>
>
> Has any one of you faced similar problems? what is the way out?
>
>
>
Yes , I have .
Most likely it is a combination of many issues.

It starts with poor earthing and some component form the motherboard
touching your cabinet.
Components touching the cabinet is not a light issue as it short circuits
many things.
Due to redundancy and good design of manufacturers , the issue is bypassed
and doesn't come to your notice initially.
The cause of such short circuits is  using a poorly mocked up cheap cabinet
of a good brand or not using the right screws to pin it(cabinets come with
special screws to attach motherboards)  ,  or not using an insulation layer
even if it is provided with the cabinet.

At this stage ,  if you earthing is good , you won't realize it cause you
don't get any electric shocks , and it takes time to wear things out .

Slowly the SMPS  starts to build problems under such condition and the
different components in the motherboard grow weak , that is when you realize
that something has gone wrong. A usb cannot get excessive power only from a
fault SMPS , it is always through the motherboard.

You must consider getting your motherboard fixed properly to the cabinet and
if necessary to change the cabinet , if after inspection you realize that
there are electric leaks to the body.

Remember the backside of the motherboard is where the circuit is made up of
, and it is very sensitive to even small magnitude of current such as the
static electricity from your body . It really is a big concern when such a
sensitive circuit touches the cabinet .

I had 15 pc's with the similar problem and even stranger ones  because i had
compromised on the cabinet. Then I  fixed it by getting an plastic
insulation placed between the motherboard and the cabinet.

In all the situations , earthing helps.

good luck

Antano Solar John

From lawgon at thenilgiris.com  Wed Aug 29 16:05:25 2007
From: lawgon at thenilgiris.com (Kenneth Gonsalves)
Date: Wed Aug 29 16:05:50 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] mailing list language
In-Reply-To: <d16b1c80708290318t626a761aqea61e086c38c80cc@mail.gmail.com>
References: <697a2bc80708290245t4bbe4eb6je574036a4f63907@mail.gmail.com>
	<d16b1c80708290318t626a761aqea61e086c38c80cc@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <A9472BCB-FE87-420A-BF11-EB6AC2AE438E@thenilgiris.com>


On 29-Aug-07, at 3:48 PM, Shakthi Kannan wrote:

>> It would be
>> better if you post something in English so that everyone can read,  
>> else
>> people will consider this as spam.
>
> This has been discussed many times. For a start:
> http://thread.gmane.org/gmane.org.user-groups.linux.ilugc/36967/ 
> focus=37004

in my opininion, there are three types of tamil posts:

1. Where the subject is purely of interest to those who know tamil -  
for example, keyboard shortcuts in tam99, or translation of certain  
words and phrases into tamil. Or a link to some article in tamil.

2. Where the poster does not know enough english to make his point  
clear.

3. Where the poster knows enough english to post, the matter is of  
general interest to all, but the poster posts in tamil in order to  
encourage usage of tamil in the mailing list.

For the first type of post, it may be marked as something like [ROT]  
- Relevant Only to Tamil and others can filter it out.

For the second, the poster should put some indication of what he is  
asking in english, and the person replying should also give an  
english summary.

The third type does not have place in this list as it is an english  
language list - if sufficient interest is there, a tamil only list  
can be forked at some stage.

I personally feel that the first type of post has a place in the list  
as it is better to discuss the nuances of foss in tamil in tamil  
language. As for the second, it could be crutch to help people who  
find english difficult, but we have to accept reality that english is  
the language of computer science and that anyone who doesnt improve  
his knowledge of the same is going to suffer.

I have been following the practice of giving an english summary even  
in the first type of posts and I dont see why others cannot also do it.

Hi Vivek,

Thanks for the appreciation.

For our first event, we are receiving more interest from students than expected.
People are still calling me up, giving news of their successful installation of Linux distro on their boxes, some to ask doubts, some to ask for the date of next event!

While I am busy taking these calls; Koolhead17 is busy deploying Linux boxes.
The mukt.in team is still working actively on the aftereffects of the event. :)

Yes, we would love to have mukt.in again in next 4 months or so.
And we will try to have it more effective.

Thanks to everyone who directly or indirectly supported us.



vivek khurana <mailing.vivek@gmail.com> wrote: Dear Atul, Sudarhan, Pavitran and team (I dont know  names of others),

 You guys deserve a pat on the back for pulling this up. Good work guys.
 One thing  would like to suggest that let not people wait for one
year before mukt.in returns. Event like this should be repeated
atleast every six months.

 Also, I cant understand the mandatory condition of associating a LUG
for FOSS event ? LUG is a specialized group for advocating and
spreading awareness of linux. But at the same time linux is not the
only FOSS based software. What if we want to do an event for FOSS on
windows or a gathering of BSD users/developers ? Why should one
approach a LUG in such situation ? Such associations give birth to
confusion among end users, that FOSS means linux.

regards
VK

such mails from people who dont care about other's freedom but only
their's.

On Wednesday 29 August 2007 15:15, GNU user wrote:
> hi,
>
> On 8/29/07, ?. ???? ??????? <shriramadhas@gmail.com> wrote:
> > ???????,
> >
> > ????????: http://www.gnu.org/philosophy/why-free.ta.html
>

I understand that this list is open to all and not just folks who can 
read/write Tamil and have Tamil fonts installed on their resp. systems.

In my system (KMail 1.9.5), the mail headers appear with "boxes" (as 
with above quoted headers) for those who use the Tamil char. set in 
their header information.  I agree, it is their prerogative to do so.   
However, given that such lists get archived in global search engines 
and repos., IMO it would be better to use a common denominator language 
for such items.  The same applies to Devnagari, Bengali, Gujrati ...

On the subject of discussing something specific like translations or 
helping some poster who cannot express him/her self in English it would 
be appropriate to put the original thought in the "native" language 
with it's respective font but have someone translate it for the benefit 
of those who do not understand the language.

These are my thoughts - my two cents.

May the source be with you.

Regards, 
-- Arun Khan

The only reason this list exists is to promote and discuss Linux and by 
extension, FOSS. As long as the majority of the users of this list 
understand the message, it is perfectly fine (See, which language does 
not matter.. What matters is whether the message is reaching the 
intended audience, most of the time for most of the messages)

Yes, it is tyranny of the majority and forcing a language on all "I 
cannot understand that particular language" folks. Yes, it would be nice 
to provide a translation.

But won't it also be nice to ask for translation? I do not even think 
there are as many messages in Tamil as there are messages about messages 
in Tamil..

Ask and ye shall receive...

From prem at songbirdtech.com  Thu Aug 30 10:03:41 2007
From: prem at songbirdtech.com (Prem Kurian Philip)

Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Re: mailing list language

If the aims of this list is to target even those people who do not
understand / write English but who are familiar with Tamil, I think it is
fine to allow these people to write their questions in Tamil.

That will mean that a lot of people in this list won't understand the
question (including myself) and will have to ignore the email and carry
on. And that is ok, because there are obviously people who do read tamil
on this list and are capable of replying.

I know that some people who are fully conversant in English would also opt
to write in Tamil knowing fully well that by doing so, they are basically
excluding a lot of people on this list. Whether this is right is
debatable.

I think it would help if people who know English write their
comments/questions in English, but the list must remain open to those who
don't know English and who may write in Tamil.

Regards,
PK


From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Thu Aug 30 10:35:07 2007
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Thu Aug 30 10:25:56 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] LJ Tech Tip
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0708301031320.1816-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

LJ Tech Tip on Taking Screenshots:

Taking screenshots on your Linux desktop is one of the most powerful
techniques that can come in handy on a rainy day. The simplest way to
achieve this end is typing this:

  $ xwd -out /tmp/shot.xwd

And then select the window you want to "photograph" with your mouse
pointer. If you wish to capture the root window:

  $ xwd -root -out /tmp/rootwin.xwd

Typically you would invoke xwd from a different virtual desktop and
use the keyboard to switch to the desktop in which the target window
lies. This is to avoid overlapping windows occluding the target
window. Once you obtain the dump, convert will help you convert to the
format of choice.

  $ convert /tmp/shot.xwd ~/shots/xterm.png
    or
  $ convert /tmp/shot.xwd ~/shots/xterm.jpg

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S

??????? wrote:
> bye the it ok to have funku bunky names..  amachu, teknofreak,
> lawgon, shakthimaan etc., etc.,

Though not to digress too much, I just want to point that these are
not just funky bunky names but nicks that are known and recognized in
the worldwide community. People mostly call Kenneth as lawgon, they
immediately recognize me and Shkathi when we say technofreak and
shakthimaan/mbuf respectively. IMHO, nicks are more than funky bunky
names, it is our identity in the community without our original
identity of nation, caste, etc being revealed. Second thing, it is
easier for people to remember our nicks than our names :)

Back to the OT, this issue was once raised by same me and it was
resolved (hope so) that posts can be in tamil provided they have a
[Tamil] tag, and either the OP or someone who is able to understand
what it is cares to posting the same post in tamil so as not tamil
members can also know what it is. Though this post was about a
document translated in tamil, which of course non-tamil members would
not have been able to read, if the message was posted also in English
they would have at least known that the translation of such a document
has been done in Tamil, and might point it to people in future.

I humbly request,
[1] Who ever posts in Tamil, please also try to give the same message
in English as much as possible.
[2] If you feel English is too bad to get embarrassed, post your query
in Tamil but still post the same in whatever English you know because
we can also help you to improve your English as well (may be some one
of us might privately post you with the right way to ask the same ;) )
[3] Non-Tamil readers, please do not discourage posting in Tamil
because as a Local LUG it is equally important for us to improve
documentation and resources in native language as well.

Hope this thread ends here and above requests are full filled :)

From prem at songbirdtech.com  Thu Aug 30 22:04:22 2007
From: prem at songbirdtech.com (Prem Kurian Philip)
Date: Thu Aug 30 22:04:35 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Re: Re: mailing list language
Message-ID: <49592.61.247.255.57.1188491662.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>

>> I think it would help if people who know English write their
>> comments/questions in English, but the list must remain open
>> to those who don't know English and who may write in Tamil.
>>
>> Regards,
>> PK

> I think there is no lugc member who knows only Tamil and does not
> know English.

Yes, but there may be people who may just register into this site just to
get one or two of their questions answered, and these people may not know
passable English.

>From my experience with working with organizations in the smaller towns,
most of the people doing the system administration (those who require the
services of a mailing list like ilugc) know very little English.

It doesn't make sense to ask them to post in English as well.

I don't claim to speak for everyone, but as for myself, I am not too
bothered by the Tamil language posts on this list. Only a minority of
posts are in Tamil, and I don't think I am losing much by not
understanding them.

As for whether these Tamil posts are using up my valuable bandwidth, well
- there are enough posts in English on this list which may not be exactly
on the topics I am interested in hearing about. So if I count all the
posts in English that I ignore because it is not of interest to me and
compare that against the number of posts in Tamil, I am sure the posts in
tamil are far fewer.

Regards,
PK

I am trying to understand the following things regarding LVM...

	1. How much role does an partition type play in the kernel
initialization phase...? 

	2.does the kernel only initialize physical volumes of type 8e during
system boot up? 

	3. If yes, they when are physical volumes belonging to LVM of non 8e
type get initialized? they do work like this... I have seen them and
hence this mail..

	4. If no, then what is the normal LVM PV?VG initialization procedure...
my understanding was that VG are initialized by the kernel once the
dm-mapper is loaded into the memory.. which is generally done towards
the end of kernel initialization or during the initial phase of system
boot up..

my assumption was that, the partition type actually helps the kernel
read the initial FS/partition structures. 

Can anybody help me in clearing the clouds in my brain..?

Kiran

K. Sai Kiran wrote:
> 	1. How much role does an partition type play in the kernel
> initialization phase...? 
>
>   
None. As long as you have appropriate module loaded during the boot up 
process, everything will play along nicely. This is true even for EFI 
architecture and any other architecture. All it needed is to properly 
recognize(meaning respective kernel modules) the underlaying H/W 
architecture
> 	2.does the kernel only initialize physical volumes of type 8e during
> system boot up? 
>
>   
Refer to answer #1
> 	3. If yes, they when are physical volumes belonging to LVM of non 8e
> type get initialized? they do work like this... I have seen them and
> hence this mail..
>
>   
When the respective module is loaded and asked for initialization by the 
kernel.
> 	4. If no, then what is the normal LVM PV?VG initialization procedure...
> my understanding was that VG are initialized by the kernel once the
> dm-mapper is loaded into the memory.. which is generally done towards
> the end of kernel initialization or during the initial phase of system
> boot up..
>
>   
If you do not have the lvm modules in your initrd image, then you will 
need to load them manually. This could in case of where your root fs is 
not on lvm.

> my assumption was that, the partition type actually helps the kernel
> read the initial FS/partition structures. 
>
>   
No, it is the kernel modules helps the kernel load and use the partitions.

HTH.
Chandra
>

Message-ID: <20070831041520.GA19808@localhost>

On Fri, Aug 31, 2007 at 09:32:04AM +0530, Arnold Noronha wrote:
> Also, I am not sure, but I don't think that POP3 connections can go
> via a HTTP proxy... you'll want to configure IP forwarding on the
> server...

Yes, you are correct. In the default settings, the proxy server usually
allows only ports 21 (FTP), 80 (HTTP) and 443 (HTTPS). This means that
any other service has to be accessed through port forwarding from
another computer, or by relaying the request through HTTP, which I
don't think is possible without some effort.

Kumar
